Language Dev. Program, Inc. v. Ambach


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Third Department


96 A.D.2d 667; 466 N.Y.S.2d 734; 1983 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 19226



July 21, 1983 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner program sought review of an order from the Supreme Court, Albany County (New York), which dismissed an application to annul a determination of respondent Commissioner of Education which restricted the ability to receive public funds.


OVERVIEW: The program challenged an order which dismissed an application and denied a motion for leave to reargue in a suit to annul a determination of the Commissioner which restricted the program's ability to receive public funds for the education of children with handicapping conditions. On appeal, the court affirmed the judgment and held that the program did not have a property interest or right sufficient to require a hearing before any modification of the scope of the students it could educate. It did not appear any factual issues existed for resolution at a hearing because the Commissioner did nothing more than implement a policy measure in accordance with classifications contained in the regulations then in effect.


OUTCOME: An order of the lower court dismissing the program's suit against the Commissioner was affirmed.

 

843 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


In re Adoption of Landaverde


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, First Department


95 A.D.2d 29; 465 N.Y.S.2d 6; 1983 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 18514



July 14, 1983 



DISPOSITION: Orders of the Family Court of the State of New York, New York County, entered on March 31, 1982, May 28, 1982 and August 20, 1982, respectively, affirmed, without costs and without disbursements.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Family Court, New York County (New York) granted an application by petitioner natural mother for custody of her son, and denied the petition of respondent custodians for custody and adoption of the child.


OVERVIEW: At the time of the child's birth, the natural mother placed the child with the custodial parents, but retained custody, control, earnings and support of the child. Three weeks later, the natural mother began to demand the return of her infant, leading to her petitioner to regain custody. The court held that there was no basis for the state to intervene in the natural mother's right to custody of her child because there was no showing of surrender, abandonment, unfitness, persistent neglect, unfortunate or involuntary extended disruption of custody, or other extraordinary circumstances. The mother was dedicated to the struggle to regain her child, and the delay in returning the child to her was largely caused by protracted court proceedings. The period of separation was entitled to little, if any, consideration because it was due to the custodians' efforts to gain custody. The natural mother's poverty did not disqualify her from successful parenting. There were no extraordinary circumstances that would drastically affect the welfare of the child that required court intervention in the mother's right to custody.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the orders that granted the mother the custody of her son.


HEADNOTES

Parent and Child -- Custody -- Extraordinary Circumstances

The Family Court properly granted petitioner natural mother custody of her infant son, who has lived with respondents since his birth nearly three years ago, and properly denied respondents' petition to adopt the child or to retain custody of the boy, where there has been no surrender, abandonment or persistent neglect of the child by petitioner, who has not been proven unfit as a parent and who has been seeking the return of her child since three weeks after she placed him with respondents as proposed adoptive parents; the poverty of the mother, coupled with the fact that she [***2] is unmarried, speaks little English, is an illegal alien subject to deportation and had changed her plans as to where and how she will make a home for the child, does not constitute "extraordinary circumstances" within the meaning of Matter of Bennett v Jeffreys (40 NY2d 543) as would permit the State to intervene and make a custodial disposition on the basis of the best interests of the child.

 

844 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Russell v. Pittsford


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Fourth Department


94 A.D.2d 410; 464 N.Y.S.2d 906; 1983 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 18002



July 11, 1983 



DISPOSITION: Judgment unanimously affirmed, with costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant town sought review of a judgment of the a judgment of the Supreme Court at Special Term, Monroe County (New York), which declared unconstitutional Pittsford, N.Y. Code of Ordinances § 11-11(a).


OVERVIEW: The florist and his employees had peddled flowers to passersby on the public ways of the town. The town enacted an ordiance restricting peddling on the public highways. The florist commenced a declaratory judgment action to challenge the constitutionality of the ordinance. The trial court ruled that the ordinance was unconstitutional. On review, the court affirmed and found that the florist was adversely affected by the ordinance and this gave him him standing to challenge its validity.The florist maintained that the effect of the requirement that he keep moving at all times except when actually effecting a sale to a customer was so restrictive as to make the conduct of peddling virtually impossible. The court held that irrespective of whether the florist's contentions were valid, it was apparent that the ordinance was so severely restrictive that it would unquestionably have a deleterious effect on his business. The town did not advance any rationale to support the proposition that such a severe degree of restriction was reasonably related to improving traffic safety and aesthetics within the town. The ordinance was arbitrary and its language was impermissibly vague.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the finding in favor of the florist that the town's ordinance restricting peddling was unconstitutional.


HEADNOTES

Hawkers and Peddlers -- Regulation by Town Ordinance

A town ordinance making it unlawful for peddlers "to stand, or permit any vehicle * * * to stand, in any place for any period of time, except in direct response to a customer's request to purchase, and then only for such period of time as is necessary to effect the sale and purchase", is unconstitutional, since there is no reasonable nexus between the town's objective, which is to alleviate traffic congestion around the peddler and to preserve the town's aesthetics, and the means employed to implement that objective, requiring peddlers to continuously move except when making a sale; furthermore, the phrase "request to purchase" is impermissibly vague since peddlers are not provided with adequate notice of what conduct is prohibited.

 

845 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Manno v. Levi


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Second Department


94 A.D.2d 556; 465 N.Y.S.2d 219; 1983 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 18506; CCH Prod. Liab. Rep. P9741



July 11, 1983 



DISPOSITION: Two orders of the Supreme Court, Nassau County, entered September 9, 1981, and September 16, 1981, respectively, affirmed, without costs or disbursements.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant complainant sued defendants, physician and drug company, for damages arising from the physician's prescribing a drug manufactured by the drug company which the complainant alleged caused her to develop cancer. The Supreme Court at Special Term in Nassau County (New York) granted motions by the physician and drug company to dismiss.


OVERVIEW: The physician prescribed the drug DES (diethylstilbestrol) to ensure successful completion of the complainant's pregnancy. Nine years later, the complainant developed cancer, which she related to taking the DES. She sued the physician and the drug company which manufactured the product. The trial court dismissed the action on motion of the physician and the drug company, finding that the action was barred because the statute of limitations began to run when the drug was ingested, rather than when the damages became apparent. On appeal, the court affirmed the trial court's judgment.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgments dismissing the complaint were affirmed.


HEADNOTES

Limitation of Actions -- Medical Malpractice -- Accrual of Cause of Action

A cause of action based upon injuries sustained as the result of exposure to a deleterious substance accrues not at the time the injury becomes manifest, but, rather, when the substance is inhaled, ingested or injected; accordingly, plaintiff, who in 1969 took the drug DES (diethylstilbestrol) on the advice of her physician to ensure the successful completion of her pregnancy and, allegedly as a result, developed cancer some nine years later, is barred by the Statute of Limitations from bringing an action to recover for her injuries. Plaintiff's two subsequent pregnancies and her series of annual gynecological examinations did not constitute a continuous course of treatment sufficient to postpone the running [***2] of the Statute of Limitations, since the "continuous treatment" exception is limited to a continuous course of treatment related to the same original condition or complaint, for the same or related illness or injuries, continuing after the alleged acts of malpractice, and excludes cases involving the mere continuity of a general physician-patient relationship. Plaintiff's contention that the defendant doctor is estopped from raising the Statute of Limitations as a bar to her action because he knowingly concealed his malpractice from her and intentionally deceived her in order to prevent her from suing him is without basis; there is no allegation that he actually knowingly concealed his malpractice or made fraudulent misrepresentations to plaintiff and the allegations do not in any way indicate the kind of actual fraud necessary to create an equitable estoppel.

 

846 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Repicci v. Sharpe


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Fourth Department


96 A.D.2d 727; 465 N.Y.S.2d 352; 1983 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 19307



July 11, 1983 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a declaratory judgment action, plaintiff property owner appealed from judgment of Supreme Court, Erie County (New York) that dismissed his complaint and declared defendant town's zoning ordinance constitutional and legal as it applied to the property owner's premises.


OVERVIEW: The property owner acquired land that was zoned residential. The town denied the property owner's request to rezone the property, and he then commenced this action seeking a judgment declaring that the zoning ordinance as applied to his property, was arbitrary, unconstitutional, confiscatory, discriminatory, contrary to the comprehensive plan and in violation of N.Y. Town Law §§ 261 and 263. The court affirmed the judgment for the town. The court held that the fact that the property would have a greater value to the property owner if zoned as an office building was insufficient to overcome the presumption that the zoning ordinance was valid; the owner was not deprived of his right to make a reasonable use of the property; and he failed to establish beyond a reasonable doubt by "'dollars and cents'" proof that the property as it was zoned would not have yielded a reasonable return. The court also concluded that the property owner failed to prove that he was singled out for zoning discrimination because there was a substantial lack of proof in the record that other properties, nearly identical to his, were treated differently.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision for the town in the property owner's action challenging a zoning ordinance.

 

847 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Sea Lar Trading Co. v. Michael


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, First Department


94 A.D.2d 309; 464 N.Y.S.2d 476; 1983 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 17989



June 28, 1983 



DISPOSITION: Order, Supreme Court, New York County, entered on November 13, 1981, unanimously reversed, on the law and the facts, without costs and without disbursements, to the extent appealed from, the constitutionality of the disputed sections of the Administrative Code upheld, the petition dismissed and the matter remanded to the appellant for a hearing to determine the propriety of the seizure of the property and the amount of taxes actually due.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city department of finance (department) sought review of the judgment of the Supreme Court, New York County (New York), which directed, with respect to contraband seized from appellee cigarette distributor (distributor), that the property be turned over to a prosecutor for criminal proceedings, or that a forfeiture proceeding be instituted, or that the property be returned to the distributor.


OVERVIEW: The distributor was a wholesale distributor of cigarettes, authorized as a meter agent by the city and state to affix tax stamps to cigarettes purchased and imported from out-of-state manufacturers. The department's investigators searched the distributor's premises and seized cartons of cigarettes bearing counterfeit tax stamps. Pursuant to a warrant, the department subsequently seized stamping machinery and the remaining stock of taxed and untaxed cigarettes. Notices of levy and sale were issued on the dates of the seizures in accordance with N.Y. Tax Law § 477. The court below found that the seizure was unconstitutional because neither the per se contraband items nor the ancillary property alleged to be merely an instrumentality of the crime could be seized under § 477, because § 477 failed to grant a prompt hearing on the seizure. The judgment of the court below, which provided the department with three alternative with respect to the per se contraband was reversed on appeal because the distributor's failure to pay or bond the tax as a precondition to judicial review of the department's actions was fatal. The court also found that § 477 was not unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the court below, which directed, with respect to contraband seized from the distributor, that the property be turned over to a prosecutor for criminal proceedings, or that a forfeiture proceeding be instituted, or that the property be returned to the distributor, was reversed.


HEADNOTES

Taxation -- Cigarette Tax -- Seizure of Untaxed Cigarettes -- Undertaking Pending Judicial Review

1. The requirement of the Administrative Code of the City of New York that petitioner, a wholesale distributor of cigarettes, deposit the amount of tax at issue or an undertaking as a condition precedent [***2] to judicial review of the seizure by respondent of cigarettes, some of which were untaxed and some of which bore counterfeit tax stamps, is constitutional; a taxing authority has the constitutional right to require a taxpayer to secure an assessment by payment or bond before litigating that liability; moreover, the warrantless search of petitioner's premises which resulted in discovery of the contraband appears to have been consensual and to have been conducted pursuant to a constitutionally approved procedure.

Taxation -- Cigarette Tax -- Seizure of Untaxed Cigarettes -- Hearing

2. Section D46-11.0 of the Administrative Code of the City of New York which gives a taxpayer the right, within 30 days of notice of the fixing of the tax, to request a hearing on the determination is constitutional; the fact that no time limit is contained within the statute for the holding of such a hearing does not invalidate the statute on due process grounds; accordingly, where there was no unreasonable delay in holding a postseizure hearing and a prompt hearing was offered following respondent's seizure of a quantity of cigarettes from petitioner, some of which were untaxed and some of which [***3] bore counterfeit tax stamps, the statute cannot be declared unconstitutional.

Taxation -- Cigarette Tax -- Return of Contraband Cigarettes to Owner

3. Counterfeit and unstamped cigarettes are per se contraband, possession of which constitutes a crime (Administrative Code of City of New York, § D46-18.0, subd c); accordingly, it was improper for the court to order the return to petitioner of untaxed cigarettes and cigarettes bearing counterfeit tax stamps confiscated by respondent following their discovery pursuant to a consensual search of petitioner's premises; since mere possession of such contraband constitutes a crime, repossession of such per se contraband would subject the possessor to additional criminal penalties, and the return of such contraband would frustrate the express public policy against possession of such objects.

 

848 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Holt v. County of Tioga


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Third Department


95 A.D.2d 934; 464 N.Y.S.2d 278; 1983 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 18903



June 16, 1983 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff victim appealed an order of the Supreme Court at Special Term in Tioga County (New York), which granted defendant county's motion for summary judgment dismissing the victim's negligence complaint based on a lack of prior notice of the shoulder condition giving rise to the victim's accident.


OVERVIEW: The lower court granted summary judgment to the county and dismissed the victim's complaint because the county did not have prior notice of a defective road condition that caused the victim's injuries. On appeal, the victim contended that Tioga County, N.Y., Local Law No. 2 (1978) contravened the Due Process and Equal Protection Clauses of the Fourteenth Amendment. The court affirmed the lower court's judgment, concluding that the law of the case did not bar the court's consideration of the victim's constitutional claims because there was no prior judicial resolution of such claims. The legislature was entitled to limit the right to sue a public entity for the negligent performance of a governmental function. The law conditioned a negligence action on the county's receipt of written notice of the dangerous condition. Local Law No. 2 was rationally related to the traveling public's protection and was not retroactively applied. Thus, there was no due process violation. Nor was there an equal protection violation because all victims were required to establish the county's receipt of notice to maintain an action against it.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court's order, which granted summary judgment to the county and dismissed the victim's complaint for negligence. The court also rejected the victim's constitutional claims against the county.

 

849 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Nuro Transp. v. Judges of Civil Court


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Second Department


95 A.D.2d 779; 463 N.Y.S.2d 264; 1983 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 18693



June 6, 1983 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner transportation firm appealed a judgment of the Supreme Court, Queens County (New York), which dismissed its petition for a judgment declaring N.Y. Comp. Codes R. & Regs. tit. 22, § 28.12 unconstitutional and declared the rule constitutional.


OVERVIEW: The transportation firm (firm) brought suit to recover damages caused by an auto accident. The matter proceeded to compulsory arbitration, pursuant to N.Y. Comp. Codes R. & Regs. tit. 22, § 28, and an arbitration award was entered in favor of the firm. The tortfeasor's counsel filed a demand for a trial de novo and a jury demand pursuant to N.Y. Comp. Codes R. & Regs. tit. 22, § 28.12. Based on the demand for the trial de novo, respondent clerk refused to enter judgment on the arbitration award. The firm commenced the proceeding to compel the clerk to enter judgment in its favor on the award and to prohibit the clerk and judge from granting the demand for a trial de novo. The trial court treated the proceeding as an action for a judgment declaring § 28.12 to be unconstitutional and dismissed the petition. It declared the rule constitutional. The court affirmed the trial court's judgment. The court held that the firm failed to meet the burden necessary to rebut the presumption that § 28.12 was constitutional. The compulsory arbitration system was enacted with the provision for a trial de novo and was constitutional because it did not eliminate a litigant's right to a jury trial.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment, which dismissed the firm's application for a judgment declaring a compulsory arbitration rule unconstitutional and declared said rule constitutional.

 

850 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


People v. Festo


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, First Department


96 A.D.2d 765; 463 N.Y.S.2d 444; 1983 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 19356



June 2, 1983 1


1 Not published with other decisions of June 2, 1983, 95 AD2d 655. [Rep.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his sentence entered by the Supreme Court of New York, New York County, after he was convicted of criminal sale of a controlled substance in the first degree, conspiracy in the second degree, and criminal use of drug paraphernalia in the second degree.


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed that the sentence imposed on him by the trial court under the then-mandatory sentence should have been reduced because a new statute provided a lesser sentence for his offense. The court held that the sentence was proper. While it truly wanted to reduce the sentence, it was specifically enjoined by law from imposing the lesser sentence permitted by the amended statute. Further, proof, although circumstantial, was sufficient to establish defendant's accessorial liability with respect to the drug-selling operation conducted by defendant's codefendant. Moreover, the court noted that the statute did much more than simply alter the punishment for the crime. It redefined the crime by increasing the weight of the narcotic drug sold necessary to constitute the sale an A-I felony.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the sentence imposed on defendant.

 

851 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Barney's, Inc. v. Department of Finance


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, First Department


93 A.D.2d 642; 462 N.Y.S.2d 872; 1983 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 17522



May 26, 1983 



DISPOSITION: Determination of respondent dated January 27, 1982, confirmed, without costs and without disbursements.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner taxpayer brought a N.Y. C.P.L.R. 78 proceeding to challenge respondent department's determination of deficiency in the taxpayer's general corporation tax. The issue was the interpretation and application of the formula for allocating investment income within and outside of the city.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer allocated 100 percent of its business income to the city, for the purposes of the general corporation tax. To avoid an allocation of 100 percent on its investment income, which was derived from governmental obligations, the taxpayer bought stock in a private corporation. Although the private stock equaled less than one percent of the taxpayer's investment assets, it reduced its investment income allocation from 100 percent to two percent. Respondent department assessed a deficiency against the taxpayer, pursuant to N.Y. Comp. Codes R. & Regs. § R46-4.0(8), and the taxpayer brought a N.Y. C.P.L.R. 78 proceeding against the department to contest the determination. The court held that: (1) if the investment allocation percentage did not properly reflect the taxpayer's assets and income, the department was authorized to adjust the percentage by the exclusion of one or more assets in computing the percentage, provided that the income therefrom was also excluded in determining net income; and (2) the statute was not an unlawful delegation of legislative power, under N.Y. Const. art. III, § 1, because it contained reasonable guidance.


OUTCOME: The court confirmed the department's determination of the taxpayer's general corporation tax deficiency.


HEADNOTES

Constitutional Law -- Validity of Statute -- Discretionary Adjustment to Allocation Percentage by Finance Commissioner

Subdivision 8 of section R46-4.0 of the Administrative Code of the City of New York which permits the Commissioner of Finance of the City of New York to adjust any business or investment allocation percentage which does not properly reflect the activity, business, income or capital of a taxpayer within the city is neither unconstitutionally vague nor an unconstitutional delegation of legislative power; where it is difficult or impractical for the Legislature to formulate a definite rule, a reasonable amount of discretion may be delegated to administrative officials; the use of the word "properly"  [***2] in subdivision 8 sets a standard which limits the commissioner's discretion in adjusting the allocation percentage, and the method of adjusting said percentage is specifically prescribed therein; the Legislature in enacting subdivision 8 recognized that situations might arise where the terms of the tax law could permit escape from taxation where it was not intended and authorized the commissioner by use of a narrow discretionary power to use an alternative method; accordingly, a determination of the respondent Department of Finance of the City of New York, which imposed a general corporate tax deficiency upon petitioner following an adjustment to petitioner's investment allocation percentage where the reported percentage was found to be a gross distortion of petitioner's investment activity, is confirmed.

 

852 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Radich v. Council of Lackawanna


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Fourth Department


93 A.D.2d 559; 462 N.Y.S.2d 928; 1983 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 17510



May 25, 1983 



DISPOSITION: Order and judgment unanimously affirmed, with costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city council sought review of the order of the Supreme Court at Special Term in Erie County (New York), which directed respondent city council president to act as mayor of the city for the residue of the term of the recently resigned mayor. The president had initiated a proceeding pursuant to N.Y. C.P.L.R. art. 78 for a judicial determination that he had succeeded to the office of mayor.


OVERVIEW: When the acting mayor resigned, the president claimed succession to the office pursuant to N.Y. Gen. City Law § 2-a. Later the same day, the city council appointed a different person to the mayor position pursuant to the city charter. The president then commenced the N.Y. C.P.L.R. art. 78 proceeding, seeking a judicial determination that he had succeeded to the office of mayor and an order prohibiting the city council from interfering with his performance of mayoral duties. The trial court found in favor of the president. In affirming the trial court's order, the court held that the N.Y. Gen. City Law § 2-a superseded and pre-empted any local law or city charter provision to the contrary and that the president was the proper successor to the office of mayor.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order directing the president to serve as mayor.


HEADNOTES

Public Officers -- Succession to Office of Mayor

1. Succession to the office of Mayor of the City of Lackawanna in the event of a vacancy is governed by section 2-a of the General City Law which provides that the president of the City Council shall succeed in such an eventuality; section 2-a by its own terms supersedes and pre-empts any local law or city charter provision to the contrary; the terms of the Lackawanna City Charter are patently inconsistent with those called for in the exception to the general rule of mayoral succession (General City Law, § 2-a, subd 3) and, therefore, the exception is inapplicable to the succession procedure contained in section 4.2 of the Lackawanna City Charter which provides for the election of a succession by the common council; moreover, excluding said charter from [***2] the exception does not contravene the general policy underlying the filling of vacancies in office to ensure maximum control by the local electorate; section 2-a merely provides for the manner of selection of a mayoral successor and does not usurp the power of local governments to select their officers or disenfranchise the local electorate.

Constitutional Law -- Validity of Statute -- State Provision for Successor to Local Office

2. Application of the mayoral succession rule in subdivision 1 of section 2-a of the General City Law does not violate the home rule provisions of article IX of the New York State Constitution; section 2-a is a general law because its specified conditions are common to the class which it creates and are related to the subject of the statute, and the fact that the class created does not include every city in the State does not make section 2-a a special law; there exists a substantial degree of State interest in the succession of local governmental executives in order to provide desirable executive continuity, to avoid the expense of unnecessary special elections, and to permit the orderly presentation of election issues and, thus, the State may [***3] freely legislate in that area notwithstanding the fact that the legislation may also touch upon matters of local concern; moreover, since section 2-a was valid when the home rule provisions of the New York Constitution were adopted, it has not been affected by those provisions and remains in effect as amended; accordingly, section 2-a is constitutional and must prevail over the inconsistent provisions for mayoral succession contained in section 4.2 of the Lackawanna City Charter.

Top Tile Bldg. Supply Corp. v. New York State Tax Com.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Third Department


94 A.D.2d 885; 463 N.Y.S.2d 558; 1983 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 18342



May 12, 1983 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant corporation sought review of the judgment of the Supreme Court at Special Term (New York), which dismissed its application, in a proceeding pursuant to N.Y. C.P.L.R. art. 78, to annul a determination of respondent New York State Tax Commission which upheld in part and modified in part notices of determination of additional sales and use taxes due.


OVERVIEW: A corporation filed a petition pursuant to N.Y. C.P.L.R. art. 78 to annul a determination of the Commission regarding sales and use taxes. After receiving a tax deficiency notice from the Commission, the corporation did not deposit the tax, penalty, and interest due nor did they file an undertaking as required by N.Y. Tax Law § 1138(a)(4). The lower court found that the omissions deprived it of jurisdiction and thus dismissed the petition. The court affirmed on appeal. The court converted the corporation's art. 78 proceeding to a declaratory judgment action in order to reach a decision on the merits. The court found that the payment of the tax imposed and the filing of an undertaking were conditions precedent to review a determination of the Commission. The court further found that as the corporation failed to comply with the statutory requirements a judicial review was not permitted.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the finding of the lower court, which dismissed the corporation's petition to review the determination of the Commission regarding sales and use tax.

Franklin Mint Corp. v. Tully


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Third Department


94 A.D.2d 877; 463 N.Y.S.2d 566; 1983 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 18338



May 12, 1983 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner corporate manufacturer challenged the determination of respondent Tax Commission of the State of New York (commission), which sustained a tax assessment against the corporate manufacturer pursuant to N.Y. Tax Law §§ 28, 29.


OVERVIEW: The State Department of Taxation and Finance (department) notified the corporate manufacturer that it was liable for uncollected local use taxes relating to its premerger sales. The department also sought penalties and interest. The corporate manufacturer challenged the commission's subsequent decision to deny its petition to revise the department's determination on statutory and constitutional grounds. Upon review, the court confirmed the commission's decision. The court concluded that the corporate manufacturer was a vendor as defined under N.Y. Tax Law § 1101(b)(8)(i). The court further held that the department was not precluded from collecting local taxes from the corporate manufacturer. The court noted that the department's action was proper because nothing more than a comparatively minor period of delay in enforcement was involved. The court also recognized that corporate manufacturer's unawareness that it was charged with collecting local use taxes did not offend due process. The court also held that the corporate manufacturer's relationship with the state was sufficient to warrant the imposition of a use tax collection liability.


OUTCOME: The court confirmed the commission's determination and dismissed the corporate manufacturer's petition, with costs.

 

855 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


People v. Schobert


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Third Department


93 A.D.2d 949; 463 N.Y.S.2d 277; 1983 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 17846



April 28, 1983 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment from the County Court of Delaware County (New York), which convicted defendant of criminal possession of a controlled substance in the fifth degree, upon his plea of guilty.


OVERVIEW: Defendant pled guilty to a reduced charge of criminal possession of a controlled substance in the fifth degree after contraband was removed from his person during a warrantless search. On appeal, he reasserted that the warrantless search and seizure was unconstitutional and that the evidence should have been suppressed. The court affirmed the trial court's finding that the search and seizure was lawful. The court found that the police action was justified because the bare informational inquiry could be founded on the fact an item was lighted and passed among defendant's group supplied. The court determined that once the officers detected the odor of marihuana, there was reasonable cause to believe a crime had been committed or was being committed in their presence and the exigent circumstances, including the possibility that the contraband might be destroyed, justified an immediate arrest and search. The court concluded that the ensuing search of defendant's person was valid as incident to a lawful arrest.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction of defendant for possession of a controlled substance in the fifth degree.

 

856 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Parker 86th Associates v. New York


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, First Department


93 A.D.2d 388; 461 N.Y.S.2d 794; 1983 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 17489



April 26, 1983 



DISPOSITION: Order and judgment (one paper), Supreme Court, New York County, entered on November 16, 1982, unanimously reversed, on the law, defendants' motion for summary judgment granted and plaintiffs' cross motion for summary judgment denied; and Local Law No. 29 of 1982 of the City of New York, and more particularly section 2 thereof, is declared to be a valid and constitutional exercise of the taxing power of the City of New York, all without costs and without disbursements.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant city appealed from the order of the Supreme Court of New York, New York County (New York) denying its motion for summary judgment and granting summary judgment to plaintiff taxpayers in their action seeking a declaration that New York City, N.Y., Law No. 29 (1982) (Local Law No. 29) violated N.Y. Const. art. IX, § 2(c)(ii)(8). The taxpayers appealed from the denial of class certification and a tax refund.


OVERVIEW: Local Law No. 29 required owners of real property valued over a certain amount to pay property taxes semi-annually, while allowing taxes on other properties to be paid quarterly. The taxpayers filed a declaratory judgment action against the city challenging the constitutionality of Local Law No. 29, and the parties filed cross motions for summary judgment. The trial court granted the taxpayers' motion for summary judgment. On appeal, the court reversed the judgment of the trial court, ruling that Local Law No. 29 was constitutional, finding that as long as tax assessments were uniform, the manner of collection could have been varied. The court ruled that Local Law No. 29 created different collection classifications but did not affect assessment categories specified in N.Y. Real Prop. Tax Law § 1802. The court found no conflict between the two laws, and, thus, Local Law No. 29 did not violate N.Y. Const. art. IX, § 2 (c)(ii)(8). Also, Local Law No. 29 did not deny equal protection of the laws under the Fourteenth Amendment because there was a rational basis for the collection classifications.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order of the trial court denying the city's motion for summary judgment and granting summary judgment to the taxpayers in their declaratory judgment action. The court did not award costs in the case.


HEADNOTES

Taxation -- Real Property Tax -- Method of Payment

Section 2 of Local Law No. 29 of 1982 of the City of New York which provides for the payment of real property tax on all real property with an assessed valuation of $ 30,000 or less and on all real property held in co-operative [***2] form of ownership with an assessed valuation of $ 30,000 or less in four installments while the tax on all other real property is payable in three installments for the fiscal year July, 1982, and thereafter in two installments is constitutional; section 2 of Local Law No. 29 creates new and different classes for purposes of payment of real property tax, not for the method of assessing said tax as specified in section 1802 of the Real Property Tax Law and, thus, there is no conflict between them and no violation of article IX (§ 2, subd [c], par [ii], cl [8]) of the New York Constitution. Moreover, the deprivation of moneys represented by six-month installment tax does not constitute a denial of equal protection; there was a rational basis for the classification embodied in Local Law No. 29.

 

857 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Anastasio v. New York


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, First Department


93 A.D.2d 769; 461 N.Y.S.2d 337; 1983 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 17613



April 21, 1983 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city challenged the order of the Supreme Court, New York County (New York) that granted the motion of respondent veteran for class action status and denied the city's cross-motion for summary judgment dismissing the complaint. The veteran sought a declaration that a resolution adopted by the city council was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The city adopted a resolution limiting the veterans' real property exemption, granted pursuant to N.Y. Real Prop. Tax Law § 458, to non-school city taxes. The veteran sought to set this resolution aside as unconstitutional. The trial court denied the city's motion for summary judgment dismissing the action and, instead, granted the veteran's motion for class action status. The city appealed and the court reversed. The court initially noted that there was a strong presumption in favor of the resolution's validity and that it could strike the resolution down only when unconstitutionality was shown beyond a reasonable doubt. The court found, however, that the resolution simply brought the city's tax collections from property owning veterans into conformity with § 458 since it limited the veterans' exemption to non-school taxes. The court observed that the fact that the city previously allowed a general veterans' exemption did not estop it from discontinuing such an extralegal or permissive practice. Finally, the court determined that the city was not required to hold a public hearing on the resolution and that its adoption did not violate N.Y. Mun. Home Rule Law § 20(3), (5).


OUTCOME: The trial court's order was reversed, the city's motion for summary judgment dismissing the veteran's declaratory judgment action was granted, and the veteran's motion for class action status was dismissed as academic.

 

858 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


People v. Aiello


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Second Department


93 A.D.2d 864; 461 N.Y.S.2d 370; 1983 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 17733



April 18, 1983 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Supreme Court, Kings County (New York) convicting him of robbery in the first degree.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of robbery in the first degree. Subsequent to defendant's conviction, the crime of attempted robbery in the first degree was classified as a violent felony offense. Defendant appealed, contending that N.Y. Penal Law §§ 70.02 and 70.04, as applied to him, violated the ex post facto clause of U.S. Const. art I, §§ 9 and 10. The court affirmed, holding that the statute did not violate the ex post facto clause even though the conviction upon which defendant's status was predicated was obtained prior to the enactment of the statute. The court held further that the punishment mandated by the statute in no way affected the punishment for the crime for which defendant was convicted. The increased punishment was inflicted only for the crime for which defendant stood convicted.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed, holding that the statute did not violate the ex post facto clause even though the conviction upon which defendant's status was predicated was obtained prior to the enactment of the statute.

In re Latrice R.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Second Department


93 A.D.2d 838; 461 N.Y.S.2d 61; 1983 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 17690



April 11, 1983 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent Commissioner of Social Services brought a child protective proceeding under N.Y. Fam. Ct. Act art. 10 against appellant, who was the paramour of the child's mother. The Family Court, Queens County (New York) adjudicated that appellant had neglected and abused the child, and enjoined him from having any contact with the child for one year. Appellant sought review.


OVERVIEW: Appellant contended that the court could not adequately review the record because the transcript from one day of the hearing was missing. Appellant also claimed that the statute that provided a preponderance of the evidence standard for proving child abuse in child protective proceedings was unconstitutional. The court found that appellant failed to raise at family court his constitutional claim that due process required use of a clear and convincing evidence standard in child protective proceedings, and thus, the alleged error was not preserved for review. The court rejected the contention regarding the adequacy of review because appellant did not assert that the missing transcript contained material pertaining to an appealable issue. Additionally, the court reviewed the family court judge's extensive trial notes and found no indication that any error occurred on the missing date.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order that adjudicated that the child in question had been neglected and abused by appellant. The court dismissed as moot the order that enjoined appellant from having any contact with the child for a one-year period.

 

860 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


In re Estate of Kummer


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Second Department


93 A.D.2d 135; 461 N.Y.S.2d 845; 1983 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 17101



April 4, 1983 



DISPOSITION: Decree of the Surrogate's Court, Westchester County, dated December 31, 1980, modified, on the law, by (1) deleting the third decretal paragraph thereof and substituting therefor a provision sustaining the administratrix' rejection of the nonmedical claim by the Department of Social Services of the County of Westchester, without prejudice to the rights of said department or Clifford and Jennifer Kummer to assert claims against the estate of Philip Kummer, deceased, prior to the final accounting, (2) deleting the fourth decretal paragraph thereof and (3) deleting the word "denied" from the sixth decretal paragraph thereof and substituting therefor the words "granted, with interest at the legal rate from the date of each separate payment of medical assistance". As so modified, decree affirmed insofar as appealed from, without costs or disbursements.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Westchester County Surrogate's Court (New York) held that respondent Department of Social Services (DSS) could recover the money it spent for nonmedical care of the children, who were removed from their parents and from the father's estate under N.Y. Soc. Serv. Law §§ 101, 104. The lower court ordered the DSS to reimburse Social Security benefits, which the DSS used for support, to the children. Petitioner administratrix and the DSS appealed.


OVERVIEW: The DSS filed a claim against the father's estate for reimbursement of care and assistance that were given to the children, and the administratrix rejected the claim. On appeal, the court held that the father, who had the means to fully pay, had a duty to support his children. The DSS was a fiduciary with respect to the Social Security benefits, and it breached its duty by expending them on nonmedical care of the children rather than utilizing public funds and seeking recoupment from the father. The lower court had jurisdiction to determine the propriety of the expenditure of the funds because (1) the federal courts did not have exclusive jurisdiction; (2) the DSS was liable to the children for an equitable accounting under state law; and (3) the lower court had authority to direct the DSS to repay the funds to the children, who were domiciled in his county. The lower court should have declined to order the DSS to repay the funds in the intermediate accounting proceeding. N.Y. Soc. Serv. Law §§ 101, 104 authorized the DSS to recover from the estate the costs of medical assistance for the children with predecision interest from each separate expenditure.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the holding that the DSS owed the children reimbursement for Social Security benefits, which it spent for support of the children, but reversed the order for reimbursement in an intermediate accounting proceeding without prejudice to a new claim by the DSS or the children before the final accounting. The court reversed the denial of medical expenses incurred on behalf of the children.


HEADNOTES

Social Services -- Public  [***2] Assistance -- Recoupment from Estate of Infant Recipients' Parent

1. Social Security benefits paid to the Department of Social Services as representative payee of two neglected infants in the care of the department were unnecessarily and improperly utilized to cover the cost of the infants' care, where their father had the means to pay the full cost of the care without recourse to said benefits, which were payable to the children by reason of their mother's death; the department should have used public funds for the infants' support and sought reimbursement of the cost from their father (Social Services Law, §§ 101, 104). Further, in a proceeding to settle the intermediate account of the estate of the father, now deceased, the Surrogate had jurisdiction to determine the propriety of said expenditures by the department, which is liable to the infant beneficiaries as a fiduciary under the common law of New York, and the Surrogate had the right to sua sponte direct the department to repay the moneys to the children, who were domiciled in his county and subject to the in personam jurisdiction of the court (SCPA 201, 1701, 1702). However, the Surrogate should have declined to [***3] exercise that power, without prejudice to the rights of the department or the children to assert claims against the estate prior to the final accounting to recoup the expenses for support of the children during decedent's lifetime, as this would permit the recovery of predecision interest on the award.

Social Services -- Public Assistance -- Recoupment from Estate of Infant Recipients' Parent

2. A stipulation settling a proceeding commenced by the Department of Social Services against decedent father during his lifetime to recover for the support of his two neglected children is not a bar to recovery by the department, after his death, of amounts he could and should have paid in support, since the stipulation expressly provided that it was "without prejudice". Furthermore, since decedent gave no consideration for the stipulation of settlement, the estate would not be prejudiced by permitting the claim for the cost of care of the children; decedent had turned over bonds to the department which were the property of his children, having been registered in the name of their deceased mother as custodian of the children under the New York Uniform Gifts to Minors Act.

 [***4] Social Services -- Medical Assistance -- Recoupment from Estate of Infant Recipients' Parent

3. Sections 101 and 104 of the Social Services Law authorize the recovery from a responsible relative or his estate of medical assistance actually paid for children, regardless of whether the assistance was correctly or incorrectly paid (Social Services Law, § 366, subd 3). Accordingly, the Department of Social Services may recover from decedent father's estate the cost of medical assistance for his two neglected children in its care, which assistance was provided during the lifetime of their father, who was financially able to pay such expenses; further, each separate expenditure by the department for medical assistance should bear predecision interest at the legal rate from the date of payment ( CPLR 5001, subd [b]).

 

861 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Montalvo v. Consolidated Edison Co.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, First Department


92 A.D.2d 389; 460 N.Y.S.2d 784; 1983 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 16633



March 29, 1983 



DISPOSITION: Order and judgment (one paper), Supreme Court, New York County, entered on March 29, 1982, reversed, on the law, without costs and without disbursements, judgment entered dismissing in their entirety respondent's first two causes of action, and a declaration made that no State action is present under the circumstances of this case.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, a utility company and the public utility commission (commission), appealed a judgment from the Supreme Court, New York County (New York) that granted plaintiff consumer partial summary judgment on her claims that the utility violated the her constitutional due process rights when it denied her application for utility services and that the commission violated those rights when it failed to promulgate rules to safeguard her interest.


OVERVIEW: The consumer was a recipient of state public assistance benefits and applied to the utility company (utility) for services when she moved to a new home. The utility denied the application because she owed for services at her former address. The past due balance was the responsibility of her former landlord, but the utility did not inform her of any procedure through which to contest her liability. The consumer sued the utility and commission, alleging that it violated her state and federal constitutional due process rights and that the commission violated due process by not promulgating rules that would have required that first-time applicants such as she be afforded procedural due process safeguards before their applications could be denied. The trial court rendered judgment for the consumer. On appeal, the court ruled that the utility's conduct was private, and not state, action and thus the consumer had no cognizable action for a due process violation under either N.Y. Const. art. I, § 6 or U.S. Const. amend. XIV. Likewise, the court ruled, the commission's failure to promulgate the rules urged by the consumer was an insufficient predicate to support a finding of state action.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment. Neither the utility company's conduct in denying the consumer's application for services nor the commission's failure to promulgate rules to ensure procedural due process safeguards to applicants such as the consumer amounted to "state action" for purposes of the consumer's due process claims. The consumer's request for an injunction was mooted by legislation that protected persons such as her.


HEADNOTES

Public Utilities -- Public Service Commission

Causes of action by plaintiff public assistance recipient to recover for alleged violation of constitutional rights against [***2] defendants public utility company and the Public Service Commission (PSC) are dismissed, where the public utility denied plaintiff's application for residential utility service on the ground that she had a past due account at a former address, without notifying her of any procedure for contesting liability for the arrears, which, in fact, were the responsibility of her former landlord; the utility's conduct did not constitute State action for purposes of due process protection under the United States or New York Constitutions, and the failure of PSC to promulgate regulations that might have prevented plaintiff's injury, which inaction was not alleged to have been willful, also affords an insufficient predicate to support a finding of State action. Furthermore, plaintiff's claims for injunctive relief against PSC is moot, legislation having been enacted during the pendency of the appeal to protect persons receiving public assistance from being deprived of utility service (Public Service Law, § 30 et seq.).

 

862 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


In re Estate of Johnson


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Second Department


93 A.D.2d 1; 460 N.Y.S.2d 932; 1983 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 17086



March 21, 1983 



DISPOSITION: Intermediate decree of the Surrogate's Court, Westchester County, dated September 10, 1981, reversed, on the law, without costs or disbursements, and the Attorney-General's petition for a construction of article sixth of the will of Edwin Irving Johnson so as to delete the word "men" and to insert in place thereof the word "persons" is granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A decedent's will created a gender-restricted scholarship fund to be administered by a school district. The school district refused award the scholarships and the Westchester County Surrogate's Court (New York) refused to delete the sex restriction or ordered that the school district be replaced by a private trustee who was willing to administer the fund. Appellant attorney general sought review of the decision.


OVERVIEW: The attorney general contended that the Surrogate's decree was both inconsistent with a proper application of the doctrine of cy pres and violative of the constitutional guarantee of equal protection of the law. The court found that by naming the school district as the trustee to receive, invest, administer, and dispense the scholarship funds, the bequest required substantial state involvement, thereby triggering the guarantees of the Fourteenth Amendment. The Surrogate was correct in determining that it was appropriate to reform the trust because the decedent would have preferred the removal of the gender restriction to the failure of the trust. However, the court held that it would not give effect to a testamentary disposition designed to carry out some immoral or illegal purpose. The court held that presented with an invidiously discriminatory charitable trust which could not be constitutionally performed, the Surrogate was precluded by the Fourteenth Amendment from actively intervening to reform the trust in a way that had the "immediate objective" and "ultimate effect" of enforcing its discriminatory provision.


OUTCOME: The court held that the Surrogate's intermediate decree should be reversed and that the attorney general's petition to construe the will so as to the delete the gender restriction should be granted.


HEADNOTES

Constitutional Law -- Equal Protection of Laws -- Reformation of Discriminatory Private Trust

The equal protection clause of the Fourteenth Amendment to the United States Constitution was violated where, in a proceeding to construe the provisions of a will establishing a scholarship fund for the benefit of needy and deserving male high school graduates within a local school district and naming the [***2] school district as trustee, the Surrogate directed that a private trustee be substituted in place of the named trustee, which, as an agency of the State, is constitutionally prohibited from administering the invidiously discriminatory provisions of the trust; the decree was itself an unconstitutional exercise of State judicial power, since it directed reformation in order to give effect to the discriminatory objective of a trust which was constitutionally infirm as originally established. The proper course is to delete the gender restriction, since it was at least as important to the testator that the school district carry out the task of selecting the scholarship recipients as it was to exclude women as objects of his bounty.

Eisenberg v. Citation-Langley Corp.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, First Department


92 A.D.2d 795; 459 N.Y.S.2d 788; 1983 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 17165



March 15, 1983 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner creditor appealed an order of the Supreme Court, New York County (New York), which vacated an order of attachment previously granted ex parte in the creditor's action on a debt.


OVERVIEW: The creditor filed an action against respondent debtor and obtained an ex parte order of attachment, which was served on defendant garnishee. The trial court vacated the order of attachment, and the creditor appealed. In affirming, the court held that (1) pursuant to N.Y. C.P.L.R. 6211(b), the creditor should have moved to confirm the order of attachment within five days from the date the order was served on the garnishee regardless of whether the garnishee was then holding property belonging to the debtor; and (2) § 6211(b) had been enacted to comply with the claims that the existing attachment procedure unconstitutionally deprived debtor defendants of a prompt hearing after an ex parte attachment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order, which vacated an order of attachment previously granted ex parte in the creditor's action on a debt.

 

864 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Mt. Vernon v. State Bd. of Equalization & Assessment


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Third Department


92 A.D.2d 985; 461 N.Y.S.2d 493; 1983 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 17404



March 10, 1983 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner mayor appealed the judgment of the Supreme Court at Special Term, Albany County (New York), which dismissed the mayor's application, in a proceeding pursuant to N.Y. C.P.L.R. § 78, to annul a determination of respondent State of New York Board of Equalization and Assessment (SBEA), which modified the penalty imposed upon respondent assessor to dismiss him from his position. The SBEA's modification called only a short suspension.


OVERVIEW: The mayor had commenced disciplinary action to dismiss the assessor pursuant to N.Y. Real Prop. Tax Law § 1522(7), for failure to establish residency in the city as required by law, for negligence in the preparation of assessment rolls, gross negligence in a tax certiorari proceeding, failure to provide adequate protection to the city in proceedings to review tax assessment protests, and attempting to persuade a public official to make false statements. The hearing officer recommended that the assessor be removed from office. The SBEA adopted the findings and recommendation of the hearing officer, but held that the penalty of dismissal be modified to a one month suspension. The mayor argued that the removal of the assessor was justified upon just cause as § 1522(7) required. The court disagreed and affirmed the decision of the SBEA and the suspension, but annulled the portion of the SBEA determination that directed the city to reimburse the assessor for back pay. The court reasoned that the SBEA determination was reasonable and no evidence existed to establish that the decision was arbitrary or capricious. Since the SBEA's determination was not unreasonable, it was upheld.


OUTCOME: The judgment was modified, on the law, by annulling the decision of the SBEA which directed the city to reimburse the assessor for back pay. The petition in all other respects was denied, and the SBEA's decision was affirmed.

 

865 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Lai Chun Chan Jin v. Board of Estimate


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, First Department


92 A.D.2d 218; 460 N.Y.S.2d 28; 1983 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 16609



March 10, 1983 



DISPOSITION: Judgment, Supreme Court, New York County, entered on September 28, 1982, unanimously reversed on the law, without costs and without disbursements, the creation of the Special Manhattan Bridge District and the amendment of the zoning resolution and the zoning map to reflect the creation of such district is declared to be a constitutional and valid exercise of legislative power, and the matter remanded to the appropriate city authorities for such action as may be proper.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent Board of Estimate of the City of New York, N.Y. challenged a judgment of the Supreme Court at Special Term in New York County (New York), which annulled certain actions of the Board, which amended the zoning resolution and zoning map to create the Special Manhattan Bridge District. Petitioners had filed the application to annul the Board's decision.


OVERVIEW: Petitioners filed an application to invalidate the amendment of the zoning resolution to create a new Special Manhattan Bridge District, the amendment of the zoning map to reflect the change, and the issuance of a special permit to a corporation. The lower court granted the application holding that the regulations adopted by the City Planning Commission to implement New York City Charter, N.Y. § 197-c, the Uniform Land Use Review Procedure, were unconstitutional as violative of the due process clause of the Federal Constitution. Reversing the judgment of the lower court, the court held that the statute was constitutional because it did not grant an identifiable property right and the notice was sufficient to meet the requirement of notice under § 197-c. The court held that procedural due process was designed to insure that there was no deprivation of rights otherwise created without notice and an opportunity to be heard. However, it was required only where it was designated to protect some liberty or property interest. Furthermore, a notice published in English in the publications specified and in conformity with the guidelines met the statutory requirements.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the lower court and declared the creation of the Special Manhattan Bridge District and the amendment of the zoning resolution by the Board constitutional and a valid exercise of legislative power.


HEADNOTES

Municipal Corporations -- Zoning -- Land Use Review Procedure

The regulations adopted by the City Planning Commission (CPC) to implement section 197-c of the New York City Charter, known as the Uniform Land Use Review Procedure, were not violative of due process in that the [***2] publication of actions designed to effect changes in the zoning map by creating a Special Manhattan Bridge District in the Chinatown district of Manhattan was published in English in obscure city publications, thus failing to give notice to a community which is basically Chinese speaking. Section 197-c created no protected property right in land use in the community, but, rather, created a right to be heard; since the statute creating the limited right to be heard also provided that the CPC adopt guidelines for its implementation, and the implementation was in accord with the statute, which provided for publication in the City Record and the Comprehensive City Planning Calendar, there could be no violation of procedural due process. Further, the notice, published in English in the specified publications, and in conformity with the guidelines, met the statutory requirement, since English is the national language and it is appropriate that all notices required by law to be published, be published in that language.

Geneva General Hospital Nursing Home Co. v. Axelrod


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Fourth Department


92 A.D.2d 739; 461 N.Y.S.2d 91; 1983 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 17060
