Montgomery Ward & Co. v. New York State Dep't of Motor Vehicles


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Third Department


90 A.D.2d 643; 456 N.Y.S.2d 274; 1982 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 18718



October 28, 1982 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner repair shop brought a proceeding pursuant to N.Y. C.P.L.R. art. 78 to review a determination from respondents, Commissioner of Motor Vehicles and New York State Department of Motor Vehicles, which suspended its repair shop registration for 15 days and imposed a civil penalty of $ 100 for violation of a regulation of the Commissioner.


OVERVIEW: Following a hearing, the repair was found to have willfully violated N.Y. Comp. Codes R. & Regs. tit. 15, § 82.5(g), which required that a repair shop provide quality repairs. A civil penalty of $ 100 was imposed and its repair shop registration was suspended for 15 days. From the court's review of the record, the court was of the view that there was substantial evidence to support the determination that the repair shop willfully violated § 82.5(g) in failing to provide quality repairs, and, therefore, respondents' determination should have been confirmed. It was also the opinion of the court that the punishment imposed was not so disproportionate to the offense as to be shocking to one's sense of fairness and, consequently, it should not have been disturbed. In the court's view, the regulation in question met the constitutional standard and the repair shop had failed in its burden of demonstrating that the regulation was unconstitutionally vague. Consequently, respondents' determination had to be confirmed and the constitutionality of § 82.5(g) was declared.


OUTCOME: The court confirmed respondents' determination and dismissed the repair shop's petition.

 

888 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Kamhi v. Planning Bd. of Yorktown


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Second Department


89 A.D.2d 111; 454 N.Y.S.2d 875; 1982 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 17979



October 12, 1982 



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Supreme Court, Westchester County, entered March 17, 1981, reversed, on the law, without costs or disbursements, determination confirmed and proceeding dismissed on the merits.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, the Planning Board of Yorktown, New York, sought review of a judgment of the Supreme Court, Special Term, Westchester County (New York), which determined that the planning board acted in excess of the authority granted it by imposing a requirement that respondent land owner dedicate to the town open space in the cluster development he proposed to build.


OVERVIEW: The planning board was granted authority by the town board pursuant to N.Y. Town Law § 281 to employ clustering for the land owner's proposed development and to modify applicable provisions of the town zoning ordinance for the proposed subdivision. The developer opposed dedicating 4.5 acres of the 11-acre plat to the town for an "open space" because of concerns that the area would become a gathering place for teenagers. The developer contended that to impose such a condition was an arbitrary taking of his property. The court reversed the trial court, holding that § 281, the enabling legislation for cluster zoning, authorized the town legislative body to delegate to the planning board power to permit deviation from the zoning regulations provided that the total density of the subdivision was maintained. The court ruled that the scope of this grant of power included the imposition of the open space condition to assure that conservation, recreational, and public purposes were served. The court deemed such a construction was consistent with the language and history of the statute.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment in favor of the land owner was reversed, the determination of the planning board was confirmed, and the land owner's petition was dismissed.


HEADNOTES

Municipal Corporations -- Planning -- Cluster Subdivision Approval -- Deed of Parkland to Town

It was within the authority of respondent town planning board to condition approval of a cluster subdivision plat for petitioner's 11-acre parcel upon the dedication of 4.5 acres of common open space to the town (Town Law, § 281, subd [d]); there is no element of compulsion or restraint upon petitioner, nor is the mandatory dedication an unreasonable exercise of the police power resulting in an unconstitutional taking without compensation, as [***2] it is entirely optional for the developer to utilize the cluster technique to build on smaller lots than would otherwise be permitted under the local zoning ordinance, with its concomitant savings in construction costs, or to refuse the opportunity, avoid the dedication condition and conventionally develop the parcel, and, in either event, he is limited to the same number of dwellings on the total acreage.

Braunstein v. Board of Examiners of Nursing Home Admrs., Dep't of Health


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Third Department


90 A.D.2d 565; 456 N.Y.S.2d 149; 1982 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 18632



October 7, 1982 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner nursing home administrator (administrator) appealed from a judgment of the Supreme Court at Special Term (New York), which denied his application, in a proceeding pursuant to N.Y. C.P.L.R. 78, to annul the determination of respondents, the Board of Examiners of Nursing Home Administrators (board), declaring the administrator's license to practice nursing home administration forfeited.


OVERVIEW: The administrator, who was licensed to practice in New York, entered a plea of guilty to the sixth count of an indictment handed down in New Jersey. The administrator was notified that his New York State nursing home administrator's license was forfeited pursuant to N.Y. Pub. Health Law § 2897(2) because the crime to which he entered a plea of guilty in New Jersey constituted a felony in New York. The administrator brought a proceeding to annul the forfeiture. The court determined that the conduct charged in the sixth count of the indictment would have constituted the crime of offering a false instrument for filing in the first degree in New York. The court explained that it was properly determined that the administrator's New Jersey conviction should have been deemed a felony conviction in New York, which required the forfeiture of his license pursuant to N.Y. Pub. Health Law § 2897(2), para. (a). The court concluded that the order of the trial court did not bar the use of the administrator's conviction in requiring the forfeiture of his license in view of the express prohibition against applying the order to a civil proceeding commenced on behalf of the state government.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court, which denied the administrator's application to annul the determination of the board declaring the administrator's license to practice nursing home administration forfeited.

People v. Best


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, SECOND DEPARTMENT


89 A.D.2d 1018; 454 N.Y.S.2d 463; 1982 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 18275



September 27, 1982 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Supreme Court, Kings County (New York), which convicted him of robbery in the first degree following his plea of guilty.


OVERVIEW: Prior to pleading guilty, defendant moved to dismiss the indictment on the ground that persons of Hispanic origin were substantially underrepresented in the grand jury pool and on the grand jury. After defendant pleaded guilty, the trial court convicted him of robbery. On appeal, the court affirmed the trial court's judgment and held that by entering his guilty plea, defendant waived all nonjurisdictional defects in the prior proceedings. The court found that the unconstitutional composition of the grand jury was among those defects considered to be of a nonjurisdictional nature. The court concluded that defendant was foreclosed from obtaining appellate review of the issue of the grand jury's composition because no state statute specifically permitted him to plead guilty and obtain such review. The court found that defendant's arguments regarding the composition of the grand jury could not be preserved for appellate review by virtue of the fact that an attempt was made to enter defendant's plea on condition that the denial of his motion to dismiss the indictment would be preserved for appellate review.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction of robbery.

893 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Corning v. Board of Elections


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Third Department


88 A.D.2d 411; 454 N.Y.S.2d 164; 1982 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 17089



September 2, 1982 



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed, on the law, without costs, and judgment directed to be entered declaring that subdivision 2 of section 8-100 of the Election Law is not violative of petitioners' right to equal protection of the laws insofar as it provides for extended primary voting hours in New York City and Nassau, Suffolk, Westchester, Rockland and Erie Counties.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Both parties cross-appealed from a judgment of the Supreme Court at Special Term, Albany County (New York) that declared N.Y. Elec. Law § 8-110(2) unconstitutional insofar as it extended primary voting hours in New York City and Nassau, Suffolk, Westchester, Rockland and Erie Counties.


OVERVIEW: Petitioners contended that the extension of voting hours deprived them of equal protection of the laws in counties where the voting hours were not extended. Upon review, the court rejected the heightened level of scrutiny test applied by the trial court and held that the appropriate standard was the rational basis test because there was no evidence that the shorter hours impeded the rights of voters in those counties. Upon review, the court found that the different polling hours had a rational basis and as such, the constitutionality of the statute was upheld.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court and found that the statute was constitutional.


HEADNOTES

Elections -- Primary Elections -- Polling Hours

Subdivision 2 of section 8-100 of the Election Law, which provides that polls shall be open for voting in a primary election from noon until 9:00 p.m., except in the City of New York and the Counties of Nassau, Suffolk, Westchester, Rockland and Erie where they are to be open from 6:00 a.m. to 9:00 p.m., does not unconstitutionally deny equal protection [***2] of the laws to primary voters in the counties where petitioners reside, wherein the polls are not permitted to open until 12 noon. A rational basis exists for the geographical distinctions made, such being that the additional voting hours in certain localities were necessary to ameliorate problems stemming from overcrowding at the polls during the evening hours and to accommodate the special needs of commuters; the fact that similar problems may exist in other areas of the State, including petitioners' counties, is not significant since legislative classifications need not be mathematically exact or perfect.

 

894 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Cass v. State


Action Nos. 1, 2, 3


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Third Department


88 A.D.2d 305; 453 N.Y.S.2d 951; 1982 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 16619



August 5, 1982 



DISPOSITION: Judgments in each action reversed, on the law, without costs; complaints dismissed as against defendant State of New York and judgments directed to be entered declaring that the Unified Court Budget Act is not violative of the Federal or State Constitution insofar as plaintiffs are provided lower salaries than granted to other Judges performing similar duties.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, the State of New York and state officials, and plaintiff judges sought review of three declaratory judgments of the Supreme Court at Special Term (New York) that granted plaintiffs' motions for summary judgment to the extent that portions of the Unified Court Budget Act were declared unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Under the Unified Court Budget Act, N.Y. Jud. Law ch. 966, § 39 (1976), judges in the family, county, and surrogate courts of certain counties were paid less than their counterparts in other counties, which they alleged violated the equal protection clauses of the state and federal constitutions, as well as N.Y. Const. art. VI, § 25(a). The reviewing court found that the legislation was constitutional. Salary classifications were proper if any state of facts reasonably could be conceived to justify the legislation. Here, variables such as different lifestyles, concentrations of population, and disparities in living costs were sufficient reasons. N.Y. Const. art. VI, § 25(a) did not mandate a particular salary structure. The State was dismissed as a party because it was immune from suit. One of the state officials was improperly dismissed because he was a proper party to the suit.


OUTCOME: The judgment granting the judges' motion for summary judgment to the extent that an act regulating judicial salaries was declared unconstitutional was reversed because it did not violate constitutional equal protection guarantees.


HEADNOTES

Parties -- Proper Parties

1. The Comptroller of the State of New York and the Chief Administrator of the Courts of the State of New York, as public officers charged [***2] by plaintiff Judges with making allegedly unconstitutional disbursements of State funds pursuant to the Unified Court Budget Act (Judiciary Law, § 39), are proper defendants in actions for judgments so declaring (State Finance Law, § 129-b); however, the complaints against the State in said actions should be dismissed, as the State is immune from any suit except where it has specifically consented thereto by express constitutional or legislative enactment.

Judges -- Disparity in Judicial Salaries

2. The Unified Court Budget Act (Judiciary Law, § 39) is not violative of the equal protection clauses of the Federal or State Constitution insofar as plaintiff Family Court, County Court and Surrogate's Court Judges residing in various counties across the State are provided lower salaries thereunder than those received by Judges of courts of coordinate jurisdiction performing similar duties in other areas of the State; differences in population, caseload, cost of living across the State and other variables might provide justification for the differences in judicial salaries, and such salary classifications do not impede the governmental objective of creating a unified court [***3] system. Moreover, said Unified Court Budget Act provisions are not violative of section 25 (subd a) of article VI of the State Constitution, which relates to compensation of Judges and Justices.

 

895 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


208 East 30th Street Corp. v. North Salem


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Second Department


88 A.D.2d 281; 452 N.Y.S.2d 902; 1982 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 16614



August 2, 1982 



DISPOSITION: Order and judgment (one paper) of the Supreme Court, Westchester County, dated January 7, 1982, affirmed insofar as appealed from, without costs or disbursements. The Town Clerk of the Town of North Salem shall publish the zoning ordinance pursuant to the order and judgment appealed from within 10 days after service upon him of a copy of the order to be made hereon, with notice of entry.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant town challenged an order of the Supreme Court at Special Term (New York), which held, in appellee property owner's action alleging that zoning ordinances passed by appellant were unconstitutional and invalid, that seven out of eight zoning amendments enacted by appellant were valid and which directed that the zoning ordinance be published.


OVERVIEW: Pursuant to a prior judgment, appellant adopted a new zoning ordinance that affected eight sites at various locations and did not include a severability clause. After protests against the proposed amendments were registered by certain property owners, the town refused to publish the amendments, thereby precluding their taking effect. A trial court held that insofar as the amended ordinance affected property in one certain location, it had not been properly enacted and ordered appellant to publish the ordinance. On appeal, the court affirmed. It held that appellant was required to publish the zoning amendments. The court found that the zoning amendments, affecting eight discrete sites within the town, should be considered as if they had been separately enacted. With respect to one site, where the owners of 20 percent of the affected adjacent or opposite land registered protests, the zoning amendment could not be deemed to have been validly enacted. However, with respect to the other seven sites, where 20 percent of the owners of affected adjacent or opposite land did not register protests, the ordinance was valid and appellant was required to publish them.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment in favor of appellee.


HEADNOTES

Parties -- Necessary Parties

1. Notwithstanding the fact that a property owner has styled its action as one for a judgment declaring that certain zoning amendments passed by a town board were validly enacted, the matter is a proceeding in the nature of mandamus ( CPLR art 78) for an order directing the town to perform a duty [***2] enjoined upon it by law, specifically, to publish the zoning amendments. Accordingly, the officer whose conduct is to be controlled is the only necessary party respondent in the proceeding, and, since the town was properly made a party to the suit, the court has jurisdiction to reach the merits; the other owners of land affected by the zoning amendments, although they may be proper parties, are not necessary parties thereto.

Municipal Corporations -- Zoning

2. Zoning amendments were validly passed by a 3 to 2 vote by the town board of respondent town, contrary to the recommendations of the Westchester County Planning Board, since the requirement of section 277.61 of the Westchester County Administrative Code that such amendments be passed by a simple majority vote was met, despite the fact that the vote did not satisfy the conflicting requirement of section 239-m of the General Municipal Law that such proposed zoning actions pass the town board by a vote of a majority plus one where the town board acts contrary to planning board recommendations; the Westchester County Administrative Code provision is controlling, since such a special statute repeals a conflicting general [***3] statute insofar as the special act applies.

Municipal Corporations -- Zoning

3. Zoning amendments that affect eight discrete sites within respondent town and were passed as a set with no severability clause by a 3 to 2 vote of the town board, should be considered as if they had been separately enacted for purposes of section 265 of the Town Law, which provides that if protests are registered against a zoning change by the owners of at least 20% of the total land affected by the amendments, or adjacent or opposite thereto, the change can become effective only upon approval by three fourths of the members of the town board. Accordingly, with respect to the site where 20% of the affected land owners registered protests, the zoning amendment cannot be deemed to have been validly enacted; however, with respect to the remaining seven sites, where the requisite number of affected landowners did not register protests, the amendments relating thereto were validly enacted and the town is required to publish them.

 

896 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Brown v. Board of Education


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Third Department


88 A.D.2d 184; 453 N.Y.S.2d 883; 1982 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 16602



July 29, 1982 



DISPOSITION: Order modified, on the law, by deleting therefrom the ordering paragraph which dismissed the complaint and by substituting therefor provisions declaring (1) that section 2023 of the Education Law is constitutional, and (2) that the adoption of an austerity budget in accordance with the provisions of this statute was proper, and, as so modified, affirmed, without costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, a taxpayer and his children, challenged an order of the Supreme Court in Albany County, which denied plaintiffs' motion for summary judgment and granted the motions to dismiss filed by defendants, a school and district and its board of education. In their complaint, plaintiffs alleged that N.Y. Educ. Law § 2023 was unconstitutional after defendants' proposed budget was defeated by voters.


OVERVIEW: After the proposed budget was defeated, the board instituted an austerity budget with appropriations for teachers' salaries and items that the board regarded as "ordinary contingent expenses" authorized by § 2023. The board did not provide for interscholastic athletics, additional library services, and a marching band. Plaintiffs argued that § 2023 was an unconstitutionally vague delegation of the taxing power because it empowered the board of education, without voter approval, to levy a tax that had no statutory limit for "ordinary contingent expenses, " an undefined phrase. They further argued that § 2023 failed to furnish a satisfactory standard to guide the board and, thus, created an unwarranted and void delegation of legislative power. The court held that § 2023 was constitutional and that even though it contained general language, it was not so imprecise that it was constitutionally defective. The court also rejected plaintiffs' argument that the austerity budget violated equal protection and held that the principle of local control of educational funding justified variations in school district financing and expenditures.


OUTCOME: The court modified the order, by deleting the part that dismissed the complaint and by substituting for it provisions declaring that the subject statute was constitutional, and that the adoption of an austerity budget in accordance with the provisions of the subject statute was proper. As so modified, the court affirmed the judgment.


HEADNOTES

Constitutional Law -- Validity of Statute

 Section 2023 of the Education Law, which allows a local board of education to levy a tax to cover teachers' salaries and "ordinary contingent expenses" when the voters have failed to pass a school budget, although containing general language, is not so imprecise as to be constitutionally defective; moreover, challenges to the interpretation of what expenditures constitute "ordinary contingent expenses" are to be directed to the Commissioner of Education. Further,  [***2] the equal protection clauses of the Federal and State Constitutions are not violated because the austerity budget adopted by defendant board of education did not contain funding for items and activities which are available without taxpayer approval in city school districts under section 2576 of the Education Law, since this may reflect a legislative judgment that, by reason of their size, city school districts require a different budget approval procedure; accordingly, plaintiffs have failed to meet their burden of demonstrating that the questioned classification has no rational relationship to a legitimate legislative goal.

 

897 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


People v. Dippolito


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Second Department


88 A.D.2d 211; 452 N.Y.S.2d 655; 1982 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 16608



July 26, 1982 



DISPOSITION: Two judgments of the Supreme Court, Richmond County, both rendered October 26, 1981, affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the decisions by the Supreme Court, Richmond County (New York), which convicted defendant, upon his pleas of guilty, of two counts of robbery in the first degree. Following a hearing, defendant was found to be a second felony offender. Accordingly, he was sentenced, pursuant to N.Y. Penal Law § 70.06, to concurrent 6 to 12 year terms of imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that he was erroneously sentenced as a second felony offender because the 1972 California burglary conviction was classified as a misdemeanor under California law. The court determined that although it was true, as a general principle, that local policy might not have overridden the constitutional requirement of full faith and credit, the nature of the federal union of states to which were reserved some of the attributes of sovereignty, precluded resort to the full faith and credit clause of the Federal Constitution to compel one state to subordinate its own laws and policies concerning its domestic affairs to the laws and policies of other states. The law of the State of New York was clear and firm that one who committed a felony in New York was to be sentenced as a second felony offender if he had committed a prior out-of-state offense and the punishment authorized in New York for that offense was a term of imprisonment in excess of one year. New York had the sovereign power to adopt that policy in the conduct of its domestic affairs and the full faith and credit clause did not deprive it of such power or require it to subvert that policy in the case at bar.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions of robbery in the first degree.


HEADNOTES

Crimes -- Second Felony Offender -- Out-of-State Predicate Offense

Under section 70.06 of the Penal Law the sentencing court properly used defendant's 1972 California burglary conviction as a predicate offense for second felony offender treatment upon his conviction of a felony in New York, despite the fact that said burglary conviction was denominated a misdemeanor under California law, since that crime would be a felony in this State for which a term of imprisonment in excess of one year may be imposed and, in fact, the California offense carried a possible penalty of one to fourteen years' imprisonment. Furthermore, the full faith and credit clause does not deprive this State of its sovereign power to adopt said policy in the conduct of its domestic affairs or require it to subvert that policy in the case at bar, nor does the use of the California conviction, which [***2] took place prior to the enactment of section 70.06, as a predicate offense enlarge the prior conviction or retroactively increase the penalty therefor in violation of the constitutional prohibition against ex post facto laws.

 

898 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Niagara Mohawk Power Corp. v. City School Dist.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Third Department


88 A.D.2d 167; 453 N.Y.S.2d 807; 1982 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 16599



July 22, 1982 



DISPOSITION: Order modified, on the law, by striking the first decretal paragraph thereof which permitted plaintiff to verify the letters of protest nunc pro tunc, and, as so modified, affirmed, with costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant city school district challenged the order of the Supreme Court in Rensselaer County (New York), which denied the city's motion to dismiss plaintiff power company's complaint, seeking refund of portions of real estate taxes that were allegedly illegally imposed and collected, and granted the power company leave to verify letters of protest nunc pro tunc to comply with N.Y. Educ. Law § 3813(1). The power company cross-appealed.


OVERVIEW: The power company sought a refund of portions of real estate taxes for certain years, which it paid under protest, alleging that portions of the taxes levied and collected by the city for the school district were in excess of the constitutional limitation on real property taxes and, thus, were illegally imposed and collected. The city argued that the power company had failed to present a written verified claim to the governing body of the city school district as provided in N.Y. Educ. Law § 3813(1). The trial court held that the letters of protest accompanying the payments constituted substantial compliance with § 3813(1) and granted leave to verify the protest letters. The court modified the order, finding that it was not necessary for the power company to verify the protest letters because § 3813(1) did not apply to the action and affirmed the denial of the city school district's motion to dismiss. Specifically, the court held that because the power company's action attacked the very jurisdiction of the taxing authorities, § 3813(1) did not apply and that the letters of protest had provided the city school district with sufficient notice.


OUTCOME: The court modified the order by striking the part that permitted the power company to verify the letters of protest nunc pro tunc, and, as so modified, affirmed the order.


HEADNOTES

Taxation -- Constitutional Limitation on Real Property Taxes -- Refund of Taxes

Subdivision 1 of section 3813 of the Education Law, providing for the presentation of a written verified claim to the governing body of the school district prior to the commencement of an action, is inapplicable in an action to recover taxes allegedly unlawfully imposed in excess of the constitutional limitation on real property taxes and paid under protest. When a tax statute is alleged to be unconstitutional, by its terms or application, or where the statute is attacked as wholly inapplicable, it may be challenged in judicial proceedings other than those prescribed by the statute as "exclusive"; the invalidity or inapplicability [***2] affects the entire statute, including the limitations and restrictions provided in it; moreover, where one of the purposes of the action is to seek vindication of a public interest, compliance with the notice of claim requirement is not required and this is so even though benefits of the proceeding will inure to the benefit of the party bringing the lawsuit as well as to other parties.

 

899 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Rosa v. Kulkarni


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, FIRST DEPARTMENT


89 A.D.2d 529; 452 N.Y.S.2d 441; 1982 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 17573



July 15, 1982 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant healthcare providers sought review of an order entered in the Supreme Court, New York County (New York), which denied the providers' motion to submit respondent patient's action to a medical malpractice panel for a hearing pursuant to section 148-a of the Judiciary Law and N.Y. Comp. Codes R. & Regs. tit. 22, § 636.1.


OVERVIEW: The patient filed medical malpractice claim alleging that she suffered unnecessary pain and injury due to the negligence of the healthcare providers. The matter was referred to a medical malpractice panel. Before the hearing by the medical malpractice panel took place, the case was reviewed again, and a disagreement arose over the anesthesiologist's purported delay in reaching the delivery room. The lower court declined to submit the action to a medical malpractice panel, holding that the only question was one of fact as to the anesthesiologist's response time. The providers filed a motion to compel a panel hearing pursuant to section 148-a of the Judiciary Law and N.Y. Comp. Codes R. & Regs. tit. 22, § 636.1. The lower court denied the motion. On appeal the court held that the lower court was not warranted in concluding that there were no issues of medical malpractice alleged in the instant action, and reversed the lower court's order. The patient charged a number of deviations from accepted standards of medical practice. Also, there was a question regarding the medical consequences of the providers' alleged negligence, which was within the province of a malpractice panel.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order denying the healthcare providers' motion to submit the patient's action to a medical malpractice panel for a hearing. The court granted the motion to refer the case.

 

900 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Balogh v. H.R.B. Caterers, Inc.


Action Nos. 1, 2


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Second Department


88 A.D.2d 136; 452 N.Y.S.2d 220; 1982 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 16594



July 12, 1982 



DISPOSITION: Order of the Supreme Court, Rockland County, entered April 6, 1981, reversed, with $ 50 costs and disbursements, and plaintiffs' motion is granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, injured person and others, bought personal injury actions against defendant corporations, in a negligence action arising from a slip and fall on a dance floor. The Supreme Court, Rockland County (New York) denied plaintiffs' attorney's motion for a short continuance, dismissed both actions, and denied their application to set aside the dismissal and to restore the action to the trial calendar. Plaintiffs appealed.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs, in their negligence actions arising from a slip and fall, sought a short continuance because a witness who would testify that water was present on the corporations' dance floor was unavailable. The court concluded that the trial court abused its discretion in denying the continuance and in dismissing the actions. The trial court erred in treating plaintiffs' application to set aside the dismissal as a motion for a new trial and denying it as untimely filed. The plaintiffs' application could not be a motion for a new trial because the trial never proceeded to a jury verdict or a hung jury. The motion for a continuance should have been granted, as plaintiffs' counsel made a diligent effort to locate the witness, the witness' testimony was crucial, and the corporations would not have been prejudiced by the delay. The actions should not have been dismissed where the corporations did not request an involuntary dismissal and plaintiffs had not rested their case. The trial judge should not have deferred to the administrative judge in denying the continuance.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order of the trial court dismissing the plaintiffs' personal injury actions, and granted plaintiffs' motion to restore their cases.


HEADNOTES

Continuances -- Motion for Continuance during Trial

The trial court erred in denying plaintiffs' motion for a trial continuance where plaintiffs' counsel did not learn until after the trial had started that an eyewitness whose testimony was crucial to plaintiffs' consolidated cases would be unavailable for several days and defendants would not have been prejudiced by granting a continuance until the witness could appear ( CPLR 4402), and it was also error to dismiss plaintiffs' cases immediately following denial of the application for a continuance although no motion to dismiss had been made by defendants; moreover, in deferring to an Administrative Judge with respect to whether to grant the application for a continuance, the Trial Judge relinquished his exclusive judicial [***2] authority over the ongoing proceeding and the statutory power vested in him to make such decisions ( CPLR 4402). Furthermore, when plaintiffs later moved to set aside the trial order of dismissal and to restore the case to the Trial Calendar, the court erred in treating the application as a posttrial motion for judgment and new trial under CPLR 4404 and in denying the application as untimely under CPLR 4405, which was likewise inapplicable. Accordingly, plaintiffs' application to set aside the trial court's dismissal of the actions and to restore the cases to the Trial Calendar is granted.

 

901 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Harvey v. Finnick


Appeal Nos. 1, 2


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Fourth Department


88 A.D.2d 40; 452 N.Y.S.2d 941; 1982 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 16582



July 9, 1982 



DISPOSITION: Appeal No. 1. -- Judgment unanimously reversed, on the law, with costs, and petition granted, in accordance with opinion by Callahan, J.

Appeal No. 2. -- Judgment entered March 26, 1982, unanimously reversed, on the law, with costs, and petition granted, in accordance with same opinion as in Matter of Harvey v Finnick, Appeal No. 1, decided herewith. Appeal from judgment entered March 30, 1982, dismissed as moot.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant district attorney sought review of the judgments of the Supreme Court at Special Term in Ontario County (New York), which dismissed the district attorney's petitions brought pursuant to N.Y. C.P.L.R. art. 78, to compel respondent treasurer of Ontario County (county) to pay him sums equivalent to the annual salary paid the Ontario County court judge retroactive to October 1, 1978.


OVERVIEW: The district attorney was elected the county's first full-time district attorney and commenced a three-year term, followed by several re-elections. The district attorney requested the county to pay him a salary in accordance with the provisions of N.Y. Jud. Law §§ 183a, which the county refused to do on the basis that the state constitution prohibited compensation paid a state officer to be increased during the term for which he was elected. The trial court, in dismissing the district attorney's petitions to compel retroactive compensation from the county, held that § 183a was unconstitutional because it lacked a rational basis. On appeal, the court reversed and held that § 183a's salary requirements were reasonably connected to the state's interest in maintaining competent district attorneys, and, therefore, the constitutional challenge failed. Also, the district attorney was not a state officer within the meaning of N.Y. Const. art. XIII, § 7, hence, the salary designated to be paid in accordance with the appropriate provisions of the judiciary law was not in violation of the constitution.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgments and granted the district attorney's petitions for retroactive compensation.


HEADNOTES

District and Prosecuting Attorneys -- Statutory Compensation Plan

 Section 183-a of the Judiciary Law, which is a general law and defines a county's obligation to pay its District Attorney an annual compensation [***2] equivalent to that of the County Court Judge, is constitutional since it is reasonable in relation to its subject matter and was adopted in the interest of the State; furthermore, a District Attorney is not a State officer within the meaning of the constitutional provision prohibiting the compensation received by State officers from being increased or diminished during their term of office (NY Const, art XIII, § 7). Accordingly, petitioner, the District Attorney of Ontario County, is entitled to receive the annual salary paid the Ontario County Court Judge retroactive to October 1, 1978; although section 201 of the County Law, which places the authority to establish the District Attorney's salary in the county, conflicts with section 183-a of the Judiciary Law, wherein the Legislature established the District Attorney's salary, section 183-a, the subsequently enacted statute, prevails over section 201, a pre-existing and irreconcilably conflicting provision which was not expressly repealed.

 

902 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Galaxy Rental Serv. v. State


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Fourth Department


88 A.D.2d 99; 452 N.Y.S.2d 921; 1982 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 16588



July 9, 1982 



DISPOSITION: Order unanimously reversed, with costs, and preliminary injunction granted in accordance with opinion by Boomer, J.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff apartment information vendor appealed from an order of the Supreme Court at Special Term in Erie County (New York), which denied its motion for a preliminary injunction to prevent defendant State of New York from enforcing the provisions of 19 NYCRR 190.8. The vendor asserted that the regulation violated commercial free speech rights under the First Amendment.


OVERVIEW: An apartment information vendor challenged the constitutionality of several state regulations governing its business, including the fees charged to customers, the necessity of requiring written authorization from apartment owners before listing their apartments, and the ban on naming any specific apartments in its advertising. The trial court found that the vendor would not prevail on the merits and the court on appeal agreed as to the fee question and the written authorization question. However, the court found that the vendor would likely prevail on the advertising question because the state's restrictions were more onerous than necessary to accomplish its purposes. The court held that 19 NYCRR 190.8 did involve potentially misleading advertising, that the state had a substantial governmental interest in protecting the public from deceitful practices, and that the restrictions imposed directly advanced that governmental interest. But the court ruled that the ban on all advertising of specific apartments available for rental went to a goal that could have been achieved by less restrictive means, in order to allow the vendor its First Amendment commercial speech rights.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment in favor of the state and granted a preliminary injunction to prevent the enforcement of the advertising portions of the challenged regulation.


HEADNOTES

Constitutional Law -- Validity of Statute -- Regulation of Apartment Information Vendors

1. Plaintiff apartment information vendor was properly denied a preliminary injunction enjoining the Secretary of State from enforcing the provisions of article 12-C of the Real Property Law and related rules limiting the fees that it may charge (Real Property Law, § 446-c, subds 2, 5) and requiring it to obtain written authorization from an apartment owner before listing an apartment (19 NYCRR 190.6 [a]), since plaintiff has failed to show a likelihood that it will ultimately meet the heavy burden of establishing the unconstitutionality of said provisions in its action for declaratory judgment.

Constitutional Law -- Freedom of Speech -- Regulation of Commercial Speech

2. Plaintiff apartment information [***2] vendor is entitled to a preliminary injunction enjoining defendant Secretary of State from enforcing the restriction imposed on its advertising by 19 NYCRR 190.8, which provides that "No apartment information vendor shall place any advertisements for specific apartments" and that "Advertisements shall be limited to the vendor's name, address, telephone number and business hours, and a description of the services offered", since defendant has not shown that its interest cannot be advanced by less restrictive means and there is a strong likelihood that plaintiff will ultimately succeed in obtaining a judgment declaring that the ban on the advertising of specific apartments violates the First and Fourteenth Amendments of the United States Constitution insofar as they protect commercial speech; although it is less onerous to enforce a ban on potentially deceptive advertisements than to police them, this is not a valid reason for imposing such a ban.

Colonie Theater v. Schenectady


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, THIRD DEPARTMENT


89 A.D.2d 631; 453 N.Y.S.2d 94; 1982 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 17741



July 1, 1982 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, the city of Schenectady, appealed a judgment by the Supreme Court at Special Term Schenectady County (New York), granting petitioner theater's application to permanently enjoin city from suspending or revoking petitioner theater's license pursuant to City of Schenectady, N.Y. Ordinance No. 79-23A, § 5-4, premised on a finding that § 5-4 was unconstitutional as a prior restraint of speech in violation of U.S. Const. amend. 1.


OVERVIEW: Appellant, the city of Schenectady (city) sought review of the grant of petitioner theater's application to permanently enjoin city from suspending or revoking petitioner theater's license pursuant to City of Schenectady, N.Y. Ordinance No. 79-23A, § 5-4, premised on a finding that § 5-4 was unconstitutional as applied to petitioner theater as a prior restraint of speech violative of U.S. Const. amends. 1 and 14. The court held that city could not prohibit future conduct that might be protected by U.S. Const. amend. 1 based on a finding that petitioner theater engaged in prohibited and unprotected conduct. The court also held that a statutory scheme whereby petitioner theater's right to show films in the future was curtailed or terminated based upon the content of films it had exhibited in the past was unconstitutional. Accordingly, judgment in favor of petitioner theater was affirmed.


OUTCOME: Judgment granting petitioner theater's application for permanent injunction was affirmed because appellant city of Schenectady was precluded from terminating petitioner theater's right to show films in the future based on content of films it had exhibited in the past.

 

904 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Golden v. Tully


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Third Department


88 A.D.2d 1058; 452 N.Y.S.2d 748; 1982 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 17481



June 17, 1982 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner nonresident taxpayers sought judicial review of the determination of respondent New York State Tax Commission that sustained a notice of deficiency against the nonresident taxpayers arising from the disallowance of the deduction that they attempted to claim for the relocation expenses incurred in a job-related transfer.


OVERVIEW: The nonresident taxpayers sought to deduct from their state income tax the moving expenses that they incurred in a job-related move to another state. The Tax Commission made a determination that disallowed the deduction under N.Y. Tax Law § 632. The nonresident taxpayers sought judicial review, contending that § 632 violated the Privileges and Immunities Clause of the federal Constitution. The nonresident taxpayers prevailed. The nonresident taxpayers carried their burden of proof in the proceedings. The modern rule under the Privileges and Immunities Clause forbade discrimination against citizens of other states where there was no substantial reason for the discrimination beyond the mere fact that they were citizens of other states. The Privileges and Immunities Clause did not require absolute equality. Instead, the question was whether the distinction between residents and nonresidents was a reasonable one, based upon "valid independent reasons." The Tax Commission's distinction lacked the necessary support. The moving expense deduction was not peculiarly related to the factors of employment, residence, or life within the state.


OUTCOME: The court annulled the determination of the Tax Commission and remitted the matter to it for further proceedings not inconsistent herewith.

 

905 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


American Cyanamid Co. v. Public Service Com.


Action Nos. 1, 2


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Third Department


88 A.D.2d 1063; 452 N.Y.S.2d 744; 1982 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 17483



June 17, 1982 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a consolidated appeal, petitioner energy association members appealed the judgment of the Supreme Court at Special Term (New York), which granted defendant state public service commission's motion to dismiss.


OVERVIEW: The association members sought to annul the determination of the commission because the recommending commissioner participated in the final decision. The court found that the association presented no sound reason why such a prohibition should, by implication, be read into N.Y. Pub. Serv. Law § 11. Similarly without merit, according to the court, was the association's further contention that the procedures followed by the commission denied the association its constitutional right to procedural due process. The commissioner's recommended decision had no binding effect but was merely a preliminary step in the decision-making procedure that served to aid the commission in making a final determination. Such being the case, the recommended decision could not be properly analogized to a decision by a trial judge who was not permitted to review his own decision. Thus, the decision was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The judgements of dismissal were affirmed.

 

906 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


State v. Strong Oil Co.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Second Department


87 A.D.2d 374; 451 N.Y.S.2d 437; 1982 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 16163



June 14, 1982 



DISPOSITION: Appeal by Strong Oil Company from a decision of the Supreme Court, Suffolk County, dated October 23, 1980, dismissed, without costs or disbursements. No appeal lies from a decision. Appeal and cross appeal from an order of the same court dated November 12, 1980, dismissed, without costs or disbursements (see Matter of Aho, 39 NY2d 241, 248). Cross appeal from a judgment of the same court dated December 1, 1980, dismissed, without costs or disbursements. Strong Oil Company was not aggrieved by the judgment. Upon appeal by petitioner, judgment of the same court dated December 1, 1980, affirmed, without costs or disbursements.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner state appealed the decision of the Suffolk County Supreme Court (New York), which dismissed its action to enjoin and restrain defendant oil company from engaging in certain business practices. The trial court held that N.Y. Gen. Bus. Law § 396-r had been preempted by and was in conflict with the Emergency Petroleum Allocation Act of 1973 (EPAA), 15 U.S.C.S. § 751 et seq.


OVERVIEW: Congress enacted the EPAA in 1973 to established federal price control authority over certain oil products. An amendment to the act authorized the President to exempt petroleum products from fuel controls and to convert such controls from mandatory to standby status. 15 U.S.C.S. § 760a. In 1979 the New York State Legislature enacted N.Y. Gen. Bus. Law § 396-r to discourage price gouging by merchants selling oil to be used for home heating. When a consumer complained of the oil company's price, the state brought an action alleging that the oil company's price grossly exceeded prevailing prices and was unconscionably excessive under § 396-r. On appeal, the court affirmed. By regulation, residential fuel oil had been exempted from federal price controls in an effort to reach an unregulated market. The court agreed that by occupying the field and specifically exempting heating oil, Congress left no room for state regulation. New York's regulation was both preempted by and in conflict with the federal law and thus, was unconstitutional at the time on the facts of the case. The state law therefore fell under the Supremacy Clause of the Constitution, U.S. Const. art. VI, §2.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court in favor of the oil company in the state's action to restrain its pricing under a state law that was preempted by the EPAA.


HEADNOTES

Constitutional Law -- Supremacy Clause -- Federal Pre-emption of Heating Oil Prices

The provisions of section 396-r of the [***2] General Business Law, which impose civil penalties upon merchants charging grossly or unconscionably excessive prices for essential consumer goods and services during periods of abnormal disruption of the market, as applied to prices charged by defendant for heating oil in January of 1980, are in direct conflict with the then existing Federal regulatory scheme for heating oils under the Emergency Petroleum Allocation Act (EPAA) (US Code, tit 15, § 751 et seq.), which established Federal price control authority over certain oil products; Congress, by occupying the field and specifically exempting heating oil from regulation, left no room for State regulation and the State law must therefore fall under the supremacy clause of the Constitution (US Const, art VI, § 2). Moreover, since application of the New York statute to defendant had a penal effect, the law at the time the underlying events occurred must govern, and the case cannot be resolved by a declaration that Federal pre-emption ceased when the Federal program ended.

 

907 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Leichter v. Barber


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Third Department


88 A.D.2d 1029; 451 N.Y.S.2d 899; 1982 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 17447



June 3, 1982 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayer challenged certain procedures employed by defendant New York State Job Incentive Board in granting tax credits against the payment of corporate franchise taxes. The taxpayer appealed from an order of the Supreme Court at Special Term, Albany County (New York), which granted a motion to dismiss the complaint for lack of standing.


OVERVIEW: The New York State Job Incentive Board was created in 1968 to encourage industrial and other business enterprises to locate, expand, and improve facilities in economically under privileged urban areas and to provide job opportunities and job training programs for residents of such areas. In pursuit of those goals, the board was empowered to grant tax credits against the state franchise tax to eligible corporations by N.Y. Com. Law § 118. The taxpayer challenged the granting of credits, and his complaint was dismissed for lack of standing. In reversing, the court stated that an examination of the complaint revealed that the taxpayer did not challenge the board's actions as being an abuse of discretion, but rather alleged that granting the tax credits was beyond the scope of the board's authority, and was violative of constitutional and statutory provisions. Common-law standing was appropriate, as citizen taxpayers had common-law standing to challenge as unconstitutional both revenue expending and revenue raising acts of government.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order granting the board's motion to dismiss, on the law, without costs, and the motion to dismiss the taxpayer's complaint was denied.

 

908 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


People ex rel. Office of Rent Admin. v. Berry Estates


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Second Department


87 A.D.2d 161; 450 N.Y.S.2d 845; 1982 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 16128



June 1, 1982 



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Supreme Court, Rockland County, entered July 28, 1981, affirmed, with costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant landlords in two consolidated actions sought review of orders of the Supreme Court, Rockland County (New York), which held that the rent control provisions of the Emergency Tenant Protection Act of 1974 (ETPA), N.Y. Laws 1974, ch. 57, were constitutional, and granted the motion of respondent New York State Division of Housing and Community Renewal to temporarily enjoin the landlords from violating the ETPA.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the landlords challenged the trial court's finding that the ETPA was not unconstitutional, and sought a declaration with respect to the initial legal regulated rent on their properties. On appeal, the court held (1) in consideration of the notice of the public hearing as a prerequisite to the implementation of rent controls, the landlords' due process rights were not violated by the lack of actual notice in the invocation of a local housing emergency under the ETPA, (2) the ETPA, under N.Y. Laws 1974, ch. 57, § 9a, did not deprive the landlords of equal protection of the laws by treating them differently than owners of other apartments that were never subject to the Emergency Housing Rent Control Law, N.Y. Laws 1946, ch. 274, § 17, as amended, (3) the landlords were not entitled to unusual remedies to change the date in which the initial legal regulated rent applicable to the landlords was determined, and (4) the division did not waive the 60-day time limitation of N.Y. Laws 1974, ch. 57, § 9a under which the landlords seeking an adjustment of the initial legal regulated rent were required to file an application.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's orders.


HEADNOTES

Landlord and Tenant -- Rent Regulation

1. The notice provisions of the Emergency Tenant Protection Act (L 1974, ch 576) (ETPA) do not violate the due process rights of plaintiff landlords, since notice of a public hearing, which is a prerequisite for the declaration of a local housing emergency (ETPA, § 3, subd [***2] c) is notice reasonably calculated to apprise landlords of the adoption of a village resolution declaring an emergency which would invoke the ETPA; due process does not require that each affected landlord be individually notified of the invocation of the ETPA. Furthermore, plaintiffs were on constructive notice of such action, since the village had previously invoked the ETPA and legal challenges to the validity of that action were still pending in the courts, and the landlords had also obtained a copy of the local resolution within 60 days of its adoption, the time in which an owner may apply for an adjustment of the initial legal regulated rent under subdivision a of section 9 of the ETPA.

Landlord and Tenant -- Rent Regulation

2. The provisions of section 9 of the Emergency Tenant Protection Act (L 1974, ch 576) (ETPA) do not deny landlords due process because of a lack of notice, nor do they deprive them of equal protection; the different treatment of landlords and tenants under section 9 of the ETPA is negligible and has a rational basis, since, inasmuch as the purpose of the ETPA is to prevent the exaction of unwarranted and excessive rent increases which would result [***3] from a shortage in housing, it is understandable that tenants would be afforded greater protection thereunder than the owners of such housing.

Landlord and Tenant -- Rent Regulation

3. Plaintiff landlords are not entitled to a judgment declaring that the initial legal regulated rent applicable to their property on the effective date of rent regulation under a village resolution invoking the Emergency Tenant Protection Act (L 1974, ch 576) be deemed the fair market rental on that date, rather than the rents fixed under an invalid prior resolution that had continued in effect through the date of the new resolution by virtue of statutory stays pending appeals by the village; although a party may be entitled to "unusual remedies" when his rights are frustrated by "calculated action" of municipal authorities, here the appeal process relative to the prior resolution was not unduly slow and landlords did not adduce proof that the village deliberately or negligently stalled the process of the appeal so as to frustrate the legitimate pursuits of the landlords. Furthermore, the landlords failed to take steps to hasten the decision of the appeal, which they could have done by intervening [***4] as of right in the appeal and either moving to vacate the statutory stay or to dismiss the appeal as abandoned if it was not timely perfected.

Landlord and Tenant -- Rent Regulation

4. A village resolution invoking the Emergency Tenant Protection Act (L 1974, ch 576) (ETPA), passed while rents were regulated under a prior, invalidated resolution that continued in effect by reason of statutory stays pending appeals by the village, was not a "backstop" resolution which would take effect only if, and when, the validity of the prior resolution was determined adversely to the village, although the result was that the rents established under the prior resolution continued under the new one; the effective date of the resolution was the first day of the month following the declaration of a housing emergency by the village, as that prescribed by subdivision a of section 6 of the ETPA, which statutorily prescribed effective date cannot be varied by the municipality or by the New York State Division of Housing and Community Renewal.

Courts -- Law of the Case

5. The "law of the case" rule applies only to courts of co-ordinate jurisdiction and not to an appellate court;  [***5] accordingly, the trial court's determination as to the legal effect of a village resolution does not constitute the law of the case on appeal to the Appellate Division, the issue not having been considered on prior, related appeals to the Appellate Division.

Limitation of Actions -- Emergency Tenant Protection Act

6. The 60-day time limitation prescribed by subdivision a of section 9 of the Emergency Tenant Protection Act(L 1974, ch 576) within which a landlord may file an application for an adjustment of the initial legal regulated rent after the effective date of a local legislative resolution declaring a housing emergency, is not a Statute of Limitations to be affirmatively pleaded; such an application is not subject to the affirmative pleading requirement of CPLR 3018 (subd [b]) as it is not an "action" within the meaning of CPLR 201 and, since the 60-day period is an integral part of the application in the nature of a condition precedent, the failure to comply therewith extinguishes the right and the time limitation need not be asserted as an affirmative defense to an action based on such a right.

 

909 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


People v. Carter


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Second Department


86 A.D.2d 451; 450 N.Y.S.2d 203; 1982 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 16091



May 17, 1982 



DISPOSITION: Appeals by the defendants from two judgments (one as to each of them) of the County Court, Suffolk County, the first (against Jeffrey Carter) rendered July 29, 1980, the second (against James Carter) rendered September 3, 1980, convicting each of them of assault in the first degree, upon a jury verdict, and imposing sentences.

Judgments reversed, on the law, and new trial ordered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants appealed from the Suffolk County Court (New York), where they were convicted of assault in the first degree. Defendants claimed selective and discriminatory enforcement of prosecution.


OVERVIEW: Defendants were convicted of assault in the first degree after their involvement in a barroom brawl. Defendants alleged selective or discriminatory enforcement in their prosecution, since none of the white patrons involved were prosecuted. The court found no discriminatory or selective enforcement in prosecution since defendants were the only ones involved in the brawl who saw fit to employ dangerous instruments. However, the court reversed defendants' convictions since they were deprived of a fair trial by the improper limitation of their right to cross-examine. The trial court's stern warning of defense counsel of the legal considerations implicated by cross-examination touching on the acts of the other's clients could not have had other than a chilling effect upon each counsel's willingness to cross-examine vigorously.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendants' convictions for assault in the first degree since defendants were deprived of a fair trial by the improper limitation of their right to cross-examine. The court, however, found no selective or discriminatory enforcement of prosecution.


HEADNOTES

Crimes -- Appeal

1. The claim of discriminatory enforcement should not be considered as an affirmative defense to a criminal charge, to be determined together with the issue of guilt by the trier of fact, but, rather, should be addressed to the court before trial as a motion to dismiss the prosecution upon constitutional grounds. Accordingly, in a prosecution for assault, where the defendants made no pretrial motion to dismiss on grounds of selective enforcement, raising the issue for the first time on appeal, it has not been properly preserved for review.

Constitutional Law -- Equal Protection  [***2] of Laws

2. In a prosecution for assault, following a fight outside a bar, pitting a group of six white men against five black men, including defendants, an allegation by defendants, the only two charged, that they were the victims of discriminatory enforcement of the law because the decision to prosecute them was based largely on their race, long-standing animosity between them and the police, and the fact that the prevailing custom in the county was not to enforce assault statutes with respect to barroom brawls, is not supported by the record, which shows that the decision to prosecute the defendants was predicated on their different and more culpable conduct, including the employment of dangerous instruments, and not on any improper or discriminatory consideration.

Crimes -- Right of Confrontation

3. A defendant may inquire of witnesses concerning the codefendant's alleged participation in the alleged crime; the denial of the opportunity to make such relevant inquiry abridges the defendant's constitutional right of confrontation and deprives him of a fair trial. Accordingly, in a prosecution for assault, where the trial court sternly warned each defense counsel that [***3] serious legal and ethical considerations were implicated by cross-examination touching on the acts of the other's client, this warning, taken "very seriously", inappropriately abridged the constitutional rights of both defendants, since it could not have had other than a chilling effect upon each counsel's willingness to cross-examine vigorously and thoroughly in the area of dispute.

 

910 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Goldfarb v. Goldfarb


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Second Department


86 A.D.2d 459; 450 N.Y.S.2d 212; 1982 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 16092



May 17, 1982 



DISPOSITION: Order of the Supreme Court, Richmond County, dated September 14, 1981, modified, on the law, by deleting the words "in its entirety" and adding thereto, after the word "denied", the following: "except the motion is granted to the extent of dismissing plaintiff's first cause of action." As so modified, order affirmed, without costs or disbursements.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant husband challenged the decision of the Supreme Court at Special Term, Richmond County (New York), which denied the husband's motion for partial summary judgment in respondent wife's action for, inter alia, rescission of the parties' separation agreement as violative of former N.Y. Gen. Oblig. Law § 5-311, which had been previously repealed -- the current section being in effect at the commencement of the action.


OVERVIEW: The parties separation agreement provided for a limitation on the husband's liability to support his wife, in violation of former N.Y. Gen. Oblig. Law § 5-311, which was in force at the time. The wife later sought recission of the agreement, and the husband sought partial summary judgment. The trial court found in favor of the wife, and on appeal, the court affirmed the trial court's order as modified. The court held that current N.Y. Gen. Oblig. Law § 5-311, which provided that either spouse could waive his or her right to support as long as he or she was not likely to become a public charge, was the applicable law, and that, consequently, the support provisions of the separation agreement were valid and enforceable, because the former section was repealed by acts of the legislature constituting measures of public policy. By reason of a retroactive application of current § 5-311, the husband was insulated from the wife's claim that said provisions were illegal. The husband's other contentions were found to have been academic or without merit.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order, as modified by granting the husband's motion only to the extent of dismissing the wife's first cause of action.


HEADNOTES

Husband and Wife -- Support

Although contracts made by private parties must necessarily be construed in the light of the applicable law at the time of their execution, a contract may be affected by subsequent legislation in the exercise of the police power, or by a subsequent statute announcing a new public policy or by repeal of a prohibitory statute rendering invalid a contract violative of its provisions, and such a repeal will render the contract valid and enforceable and not subject to the defense of illegality;  [***2] accordingly, a separation agreement containing a partial waiver of the husband's wife support obligation, executed prior to the enactment of current section 5-311 of the General Obligations Law, is valid and enforceable and not subject to a claim of illegality, since the statute prohibiting such a waiver was repealed by acts of the Legislature constituting measures of public policy. In cases involving the enforceability of separation agreements, the retroactive application of current section 5-311 may be used as a shield against a claim of illegality based solely on the former law, but may not be used as a sword in seeking to invalidate agreements, on constitutional grounds, as not having been executed in reliance on the gender-neutral standards incorporated in the new law and public policy of the State.

 

911 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


In re SYNDER


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, FOURTH DEPARTMENT


88 A.D.2d 772; 451 N.Y.S.2d 508; 1982 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 17027



May 14, 1982 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner department of social services and respondent mother appealed a judgment of the trial court (New York), which found the mother's children permanently neglected and terminated the mother's parental rights using a preponderance of the evidence standard of proof.


OVERVIEW: The department of social services brought an action alleging that the mother had permanently neglected her children. The evidence showed that the mother had voluntarily placed her children in foster care and had maintained insubstantial or infrequent contact with the children, despite the department's efforts. The court held that the department had proven by clear and convincing evidence that the mother had failed substantially and continuously or repeatedly to maintain contact with the children and that the agency was diligent in its efforts to encourage and strengthen the parental relationship. Moreover, the mother failed to demonstrate that she was aggrieved by the social services statute's failure to provide for oral notification of a parent's right to an attorney and the possibility of the termination of parental rights if she failed to comply with the agreement she had entered into with the department and, thus, she could not raise the statute's constitutionality. Moreover, the mother waived any due process claim concerning the procedure under which she executed the voluntary transfer agreements. Furthermore, the evidence of permanent neglect was clear and convincing.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the finding that the children were permanently neglected and the termination of parental rights.

 

912 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Hotel Waldorf-Astoria Corp. v. State Tax Com.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, THIRD DEPARTMENT


86 A.D.2d 330; 451 N.Y.S.2d 261; 1982 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 15715



May 13, 1982 



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed, without costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state tax commission sought review of a judgment of the Supreme Court at Special Term (New York), which ordered the commission to pay interest on a refund of taxes paid by respondent taxpayer in an action by the taxpayer alleging that the taxpayer was immune from taxation because the funds upon which the mortgage tax was applied were loaned to the taxpayer by a state agency.


OVERVIEW: The commission asserted that the action was improper because the taxpayer did not join the City of New York as a necessary party and that the taxpayer was not entitled to recover interest on the refund. The court rejected the commission's contentions, finding that the taxpayer's failure to join the City of New York was excusable because the city was not a necessary party and because the city's interests were adequately protected. The court ruled that the taxpayer was entitled to recover interest on the refund because the imposition of the tax was unlawful. The court noted that the taxpayer was immune from the imposition of the tax because funds upon which the mortgage tax was applied were loaned to the taxpayer by a state agency which was immune from taxation and because the funds were primarily maintained for a public use.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the lower court. The court held that the taxpayer was entitled to interest on the tax refund he received because a state agency's immunity from taxation was not negated by the fact that the state agency's funds were loaned to a taxpayer that was a private party.


HEADNOTES

Parties -- Necessary Parties

1. The failure to join the City of New York, which, through the New York City Register, collected the mortgage recording tax imposed under article 11 of the Tax Law, as a respondent in a proceeding by petitioner taxpayer challenging the imposition of the tax and demanding interest on the refund due, should be excused in the interests of justice ( CPLR 1001, subd [b]), since respondent State Tax Commission failed to raise the issue at any time during the three-year history of the case and the city itself failed to move to intervene either at the administrative level or in the court proceeding; in any event, the city, which is merely a collection agent for the State Tax Commission with respect to such taxes, is not a necessary party.

Taxation -- Mortgage Recording Tax -- Interest on Refund

 [***2] 2. As a State agency, the New York State Employees' Retirement System enjoys an immunity from taxation independent of the statutory exemptions listed in the Tax Law for property utilized in the public interest, and the fact that retirement system property consisting of funds was loaned to a private party and secured by a mortgage does not negate this immunity, since retirement system funds are primarily maintained for a public use. Accordingly, since the imposition of a mortgage recording tax upon petitioner mortgagor pursuant to section 253 of the Tax Law was unlawful, the recovery of interest upon the tax refund due from respondent State Tax Commission must be allowed, even in the absence of a specific provision for interest in the taxing statute; petitioner is entitled to interest at the rate of 6% per annum under section 16 of the State Finance Law.

 

913 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Herkimer v. Axelrod


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Third Department


88 A.D.2d 704; 451 N.Y.S.2d 303; 1982 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 16948



May 13, 1982 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant Commissioner of the New York State Department of Health (commissioner) sought review of a decision from the Supreme Court in Albany County (New York), which granted appellant hospital's motion for summary judgment and dismissed that portion of the complaint seeking a declaration that the statute was unconstitutional. Both the commissioner and the hospital asserted errors on the parties' cross-appeals.


OVERVIEW: The commissioner initiated proceedings to modify the hospital's operating certificate from an acute-care to a long-term care facility pursuant to N.Y. Pub. Health Law § 2806(6), and the hospital sought a declaratory judgment alleging that the statute was inapplicable to the hospital and that it violated procedural and substantive due process. The trial court granted appellant hospital's motion for summary judgment prohibiting the commissioner from taking further action to modify the hospital's operating certificate but dismissed that portion of the complaint seeking a declaration that the statute was unconstitutional. On cross-appeals, the commissioner asserted error in granting the hospital's motion for summary judgment and the hospital asserted error in dismissing its constitutional claims. The court reversed the order of the trial court and granted summary judgment in favor of the commissioner dismissing the complaint because the commissioner was within his authority, the statute did apply to the hospital, and the court held that the terms "public need" and "public interest" were sufficiently defined to withstand constitutional attack for a lack of specificity or definiteness.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order of the trial court and granted summary judgment in favor of the commissioner dismissing the complaint of the hospital seeking to prohibit the commissioner from modifying the hospital's operating certificate from an acute-care to a long-term care facility.

Dougal v. County of Suffolk


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, SECOND DEPARTMENT
