June 18, 1981 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner teacher appealed from a judgment of the Supreme Court at Special Term, Albany County (New York), which dismissed her application to direct the implementation of a hearing panel report and to dismiss an appeal to respondent Commissioner of Education. The Commissioner appealed the direction that the teacher be paid pending the appeal. The teacher appealed the dismissal of her application to set aside a determination terminating her.


OVERVIEW: The teacher was charged with incompetency, inefficiency, and incapacity. A hearing panel found that termination was not justified and recommended that she be suspended without pay and that she be reassigned. The school board was granted a stay of the recommended penalty by the Commissioner, which ruled in favor of the board, annulling the hearing panel's recommendation and authorizing the district to terminate the teacher. The teacher argued that the Commissioner lacked jurisdiction to consider the board's appeal because the board failed to comply with certain conditions precedent. The court found that there was nothing in N.Y. Educ. Law, § 3020-a (5) that conditioned the right to appeal on compliance with N.Y. Educ. Law § 3020-a (4). The teacher did not show any prejudice to her from the board's action. The penalty imposed was not so arbitrary as to be unconstitutional, nor was it shocking to one's sense of fairness. The Commissioner was expressly authorized to grant a stay under N.Y. Educ. Law § 311(2). The court rejected the argument that the trial court erred in directing that the teacher be paid pending the outcome of the appeal.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgments, without costs.

 

980 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Westinghouse Electric Corp. v. Tully


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Third Department


82 A.D.2d 988; 440 N.Y.S.2d 397; 1981 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 14719



June 18, 1981 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner corporation sought review of a determination by respondent, the Tax Commission of the State of New York, which sustained corporate franchise tax assessments imposed pursuant to N.Y. Tax Law § 208(9)(i)(B) against the corporation. The assessments were for the accumulated income of the corporation's subsidiary, a domestic international sales corporation (DISC).


OVERVIEW: The corporation, a Pennsylvania corporation, owned all of the stock of a DISC corporation, which under I.R.C. § 991 et seq. was exempt from federal income tax liability. Throughout the period in question, the corporation did business in New York, but the DISC did not. When the corporation filed its New York franchise tax returns, it did not include any portion of the DISC's accumulated income in its net income. The Commission, relying on § 208(9)(i)(B), maintained that in arriving at its franchise tax, the corporation should have combined all of the DISC's income and expenses with its own. In annulling the Commission's determination, the court ruled that to the extent § 208(9)(i)(B) required the DISC's accumulated income be added to the corporation's income, it was unconstitutional because it placed an impermissible burden on foreign commerce. The essential purpose behind enactment of the DISC provisions was to encourage exportation to foreign countries of American-made products so as to alleviate a burgeoning trade deficit. While the statute impermissibly burdened foreign commerce, it did not violate due process or equal protection.


OUTCOME: The court annulled the determination and remitted the matter to the Commission for further proceedings.

In re Northern Yarn Mfg. Corp.

983 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Conomikes v. Binghamton


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Third Department


81 A.D.2d 992; 440 N.Y.S.2d 71; 1981 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 11736



May 28, 1981 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner disabled firemen sought review of the decision from the Supreme Court at Special Term, Broome County (New York), which dismissed their application for reinstatement to the payroll of respondent city after they had voluntarily taken retirement.


OVERVIEW: The firemen were disabled and were receiving their full salary and benefits under former N.Y. Gen. Mun. Law § 207-a. Section § 207-a was amended to provide for termination of full salary and benefits upon retirement age of 70 or upon voluntary election of retirement benefits. The firemen took voluntary retirement at age 62 and were removed from the city payroll. Their benefits under § 207-a were terminated. They filed an application for reinstatement to the payroll and asserted that they had not been permitted to withdraw their election when the courts ultimately declared, in a prior action, that amended § 207-a was constitutional, because they had already reached the age of 62 and elected to receive retirement benefits. The trial court dismissed their petition and they challenged the decision. On appeal, the court affirmed and held that they had the opportunity to withdraw their election at the time the statute was amended. The determination by the courts that the statute was constitutional did not give them a second opportunity to elect to remain on the payroll.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the dismissal of the firemen's application to be reinstated to the payroll of the city.

 

984 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Archer v. North Greenbush


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Third Department


80 A.D.2d 361; 439 N.Y.S.2d 729; 1981 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 10098



May 21, 1981 



DISPOSITION: Order modified, on the law, to the extent of striking therefrom the decretal paragraphs dismissing the petition and substituting therefor a provision declaring that Local Law No. 3-1980 of the Town of North Greenbush was not subject to a referendum on petition pursuant to section 24 (subd 2, par c) of the Municipal Home Rule Law and is not violative of the equal protection clauses of the United States and New York State Constitutions, and, as so modified, affirmed, without costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners appealed from the dismissal by the Supreme Court, Rensselaer County (New York), of their declaratory judgment proceeding seeking to have North Greenbush, N.Y., 1980 Local Law No. 3, adopting the option authorized in N.Y. Real Prop. Tax Law § 458(5)(b), declared null and void on the grounds that it was subject to a referendum on petition and that it violated the equal protection clauses of the state and federal constitutions.


OVERVIEW: Respondent town voluntarily changed to full value assessment and the town board passed a local law adopting the option authorized in N.Y. Real Prop. Tax Law § 458(5)(b) to increase or decrease the amount of the veterans exemption in the same proportion as the total assessed value had been increased or decreased. The trial court dismissed petitioners' petition, with prejudice, on the grounds that it failed to state a legally cognizable cause of action and that the local law was neither unconstitutional nor subject to a referendum on petition. On appeal, the court held that the local law did not change the manner of assessment nor substitute another form of procedure and, accordingly, it did not change a provision of law relating to assessments of real property within the meaning of N.Y. Mun. Home Rule Law § 24(2)(c). A referendum on petition, therefore, was not mandated. Petitioners failed to meet the equal protection burden of demonstrating the absence of any conceivable state of facts which would support the classification. It was error to dismiss the petition in view of the fact that the proceeding had been converted to one for a declaratory judgment.


OUTCOME: The court modified the order, on the law, to the extent of striking therefrom the decretal paragraphs dismissing the petition and substituting therefor a provision declaring that the local law was not subject to a referendum on petition pursuant to the Municipal Home Rule Law and was not violative of the equal protection clauses of the United States and New York State Constitutions, and, as so modified, the court affirmed.


HEADNOTES

Local Laws -- Referendum on Petition -- Veterans' Exemptions

1. A local law adopted pursuant to section 458 (subd 5, par [b]) of the Real Property Tax Law, which provides that municipalities voluntarily changing to full value assessment could increase or decrease by local law the amount of the veterans' exemption in the same proportion as the total assessed value had been increased [***2] or decreased, did not change a provision of law relating to assessments of real property within the meaning of section 24 (subd 2, par c) of the Municipal Home Rule Law and is thus not subject to a referendum on petition, since the local law did not change the manner of assessment nor substitute another form of procedure.

Local Laws -- Veterans' Exemptions -- Equal Protection of Laws

2. A local law adopted pursuant to section 458 (subd 5, par [b]) of the Real Property Tax Law, which provides that municipalities voluntarily changing to full value assessment could increase or decrease by local law the amount of the veterans' exemption in the same proportion as the total assessed value had been increased or decreased, is not violative of equal protection as an arbitrary discrimination against property owners without a veterans' exemption, since those challenging the law have not met the burden of demonstrating the absence of any conceivable state of facts which would support the classification.

 

985 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Slocum v. Berman


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Fourth Department


81 A.D.2d 1014; 439 N.Y.S.2d 967; 1981 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 11769



May 15, 1981 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner owner and operator of a nursing home sought review of a determination of respondent Director of the Office of Health Systems Management, New York State Department of Health, which revoked the nursing home operating certificate of the owner and operator for violations of the provisions of N.Y. Comp. Codes R. & Regs. tit. 10, § 700 et. seq. The owner and operator alleged that the regulations were unconstitutionally vague.


OVERVIEW: The owner and operator of a nursing home operated the nursing home in a two-story wood frame building. The owner and operator was charged with 135 violations of the N.Y. Pub. Health Law § 2800, and of the regulations promulgated thereunder in N.Y. Comp. Codes R. & Regs. tit. 10, § 700 et. seq. The hearing officer sustained certain of the charges and concluded that the structure of the facility was not fire resistant and that the violations adversely affected the health, safety, and welfare of the occupants. The Department adopted the findings and conclusions of the hearing examiner, and held that the nursing home could not be made reasonable safe or functionally adequate for nursing home occupancy. On appeal, the court confirmed and held that: (1) N.Y. Comp. Codes R. & Regs. tit. 10, § 700 et. seq., was not vague nor subjective because the health and safety needs of a nursing home patient ordinarily would not vary with the subjective interpretations of the observer, but rather would be objective needs, reasonably-well identifiable by all competent observers; and (2) revocation of the nursing home certificate was supported by substantial evidence.


OUTCOME: The court confirmed the determination of the Department that revoked the owner and operator's operating certificate for a nursing home and dismissed the owner and operator's petition.

987 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


People v. Shapiro


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, First Department


81 A.D.2d 762; 439 N.Y.S.2d 116; 1981 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 11397



May 7, 1981 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state appealed from the order of the Supreme Court, New York County (New York) sentencing defendant to an indeterminate term of one to three years upon his plea of guilty of attempted robbery in the first degree. The issue on appeal was whether defendant should have been sentenced as a predicate felon.


OVERVIEW: The state claimed that defendant's prior conviction for attempted possession of a controlled substance in the sixth degree, an E felony, based upon his guilty plea to possession of a substance that contained at least one eighth of an ounce of methadone qualified as a predicate felony with respect to his robbery conviction. The trial court found that defendant was not a predicate felon and that the revised predicate felon statutes were unconstitutional. The court affirmed rejecting the constitutional argument and holding that the only reason that defendant face predicate felon status was because of a legislative oversight in amending the drug laws by providing for resentencing of those convicted of class A felonies for methadone crimes to lesson the harshness of the mandatory life sentences persons faced for possession small quantities of methadone but failing to provide for the resentencing of persons convicted of lesser degrees of the crime. It would have been be unfair to treat defendant's prior conviction as a felony when those convicted of A felonies for violations of the same drug laws were resentenced as A misdemeanants.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's one to three year sentence.

 

988 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Coller v. State University of New York


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Third Department


80 A.D.2d 166; 439 N.Y.S.2d 474; 1981 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 10074



April 30, 1981 



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed, with costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a proceeding pursuant to N.Y. C.P.L.R. art. 78, petitioner employees appealed from a judgment of the Supreme Court at Special Term in Albany County (New York), which denied their request to proceed with the litigation as a class action and dismissed the petition. The employees were seeking an order that respondent state employers had to continue to make contributions to an optional noncontributory pension plan.


OVERVIEW: The employees participated in an optional, noncontributory pension plan. Enactment of N.Y. Retire. & Soc. Sec. Law §§ 500 and 517 made the retirement system contributory with respect to employees hired after a certain date. The employees alleged that the change violated their state constitutional rights because it diminished or impaired benefits of their contracts with the state. On appeal, the court affirmed the judgment of the trial court dismissing the petition. The court found that the action was inappropriate for a class action because it involved government operations and because subsequent petitioners would be adequately protected under the principles of stare decisis. The court rejected the employees' state constitutional argument, finding that nothing in the application of the statute would affect the employees' benefits. The court found that the contractual relationship was conditioned upon the retirement system maintaining noncontributory status. Enactment of the statute terminated the obligation to underwrite the employees' membership in any optional plan and terminated any property interest the employees might have had in the optional plan.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.


HEADNOTES

Actions -- Class Actions

1. When governmental operations are involved and when subsequent petitioners will be adequately protected under the principles of stare decisis, class actions are inappropriate, particularly in CPLR article 78 proceedings. Accordingly, petitioners, State University of New York employees who brought an article 78 proceeding challenging the applicability to themselves and others similarly situated of sections 500 and 517 of the Retirement and Social Security Law, which changed their optional pension plan from noncontributory to contributory, were properly denied permission to prosecute the action as a class action.

Civil Service -- Retirement and Pension Benefits

2. Sections 500 and 517 of the Retirement and Social Security Law, which changed the retirement plan system for public employees, including optional [***2] retirement programs such as the Teachers Insurance and Annuity Association -- College Retirement Equities Fund (TIAA-CREF), from noncontributory to contributory with respect to employees appointed after July 1, 1976, does not violate the constitutional or contractual rights of petitioners, State University of New York employees who elected TIAA-CREF membership; although the plan is now contributory, the benefits remain the same and, moreover, subdivision 2 of section 392 of the Education Law reserved to the State the right to end payments made by the State in lieu of employee contributions to the elected optional plan, to which condition petitioners consented in writing upon joining the noncontributory optional retirement plan.

Seyler v. Regan


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Third Department


81 A.D.2d 736; 439 N.Y.S.2d 490; 1981 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 11296



April 30, 1981 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant employee sought review of a judgment of the Supreme Court, Albany County (New York), which dismissed his application, in a proceeding pursuant to N.Y. C.P.L.R. 78, to annul a decision of respondent state comptroller calculating the employee's retirement benefits.


OVERVIEW: The employee was a member of a town's police department and was covered by a retirement plan under N.Y. Retire. & Soc. Sec. Law § 87. The police department was incorporated into a county's police department, and the provisions of § 87 were incorporated into N.Y. Retire. & Soc. Sec. Law § 387-a. Later the employee elected to participate in an optional retirement plan pursuant to N.Y. Retire. & Soc. Sec. Law § 384-d. A year later, he withdrew his participation from that plan and retired. The state comptroller calculated the employee's benefits pursuant to N.Y. Retire. & Soc. Sec. Law § 387-a. The employee claimed that his benefits should have been calculated under N.Y. Retire. & Soc. Sec. Law § 375-i. The court held that (1) the state comptroller's determination was reasonable and rational; (2) there was no mechanism to permit election to the benefits of N.Y. Retire. & Soc. Sec. Law § 375-i and the employee was not covered under that plan by operation of law because his retirement antedated a change in the law that would have made § 375-i applicable to him; and (3) the employee failed to set out facts sufficient to support his allegations of discriminatory treatment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court's dismissal of the employee's petition seeking to annul the state comptroller's decision calculating the employee's retirement benefits.

 

990 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Kalman v. Neuman


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Second Department


80 A.D.2d 116; 438 N.Y.S.2d 109; 1981 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 9756



April 13, 1981 



DISPOSITION: Two orders of the Supreme Court, Queens County, dated February 13, 1980 and March 3, 1980, respectively, affirmed, without costs or disbursements.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff driver, a resident of New York, filed an action in New York against defendant driver, a resident of Pennsylvania, for a car accident that occurred in Pennsylvania. The Supreme Court at Special Term in Queens County (New York), granted plaintiff's motion to extend an order of attachment and denied defendant's cross application to dismiss the complaint and their motion to dismiss. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: In 1974 plaintiff driver and defendant driver, residents of different states, were involved in a car accident. In 1980 while the present case was still ongoing the United States Supreme Court held that in determining whether a particular exercise of state-court jurisdiction was consistent with due process, the inquiry must focus on the relationship among defendant, the forum, and the litigation. The fact that defendant's insurer chose to do business in the forum state could not form the basis for a finding that defendant engaged in any purposeful activity related to the forum that would make the exercise of jurisdiction fair, just, or reasonable. The court held that although this decision would appear to allow a grant of defendant's motion to dismiss, which was denied by the trial court, defendant had only challenged personal jurisdiction in his answer. Having failed to object to quasi in rem jurisdiction by pre-answer motion or in his answer, defendant waived it. In the face of plaintiff's good faith reliance on the clear language of the cases preceding this decision, she was entitled to protection against amendment of defendant's answer.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's denial of defendant driver's motion to dismiss plaintiff driver's complaint, and which granted plaintiff's motion to extend an order of attachment.


HEADNOTES

Courts -- Jurisdiction

1. In a personal injury action commenced by the attachment of the nonresident defendants' insurer's obligation to defend and indemnify defendants within New York, in which defendants asserted in their answer that the court lacked personal jurisdiction, following which defendants' motion to dismiss on grounds of lack of personal jurisdiction and forum non conveniens was denied, Rush v Savchuk (444 U.S. 320), which held jurisdiction based on Seider v Roth (17 NY2d 111) unconstitutional, does not require dismissal of the complaint or leave to amend defendants' answer since it does not provide a basis for dismissal motion if the jurisdictional [***2] defect was not raised prior to the motion; defendants had challenged only personal jurisdiction and must be deemed to have waived objection to quasi in rem jurisdiction, and amendatory relief is denied because of plaintiffs' inability to bring a timely action elsewhere based upon a justified reliance on Seider v Roth.

Attachment -- Insurance Policy of Nonresident -- Perfection of Levy

2. In a personal injury action commenced by the attachment of the nonresident defendants' insurer's obligation to defend and indemnify defendants within New York, the Sheriff's levy pursuant to the original order of attachment was duly perfected; a letter from the insurer's attorneys stating that a policy issued by it covering defendants was in full force and effect was an adequate substitute for the actual policy and served to repose constructive custody of the debt in the Sheriff.

 

991 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Slewett & Farber v. Board of Assessors


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Second Department


80 A.D.2d 186; 438 N.Y.S.2d 544; 1981 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 10078



April 8, 1981 



DISPOSITION: Order modified, on the law, by adding decretal paragraphs (1) declaring section 721 of the Real Property Tax Law unconstitutional and (2) declaring subdivision 3 of section 720 of the Real Property Tax Law constitutional. As so modified, order affirmed insofar as appealed from, without costs or disbursements.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayers and appellee Board of Assessors of the County of Nassau sought review of the decision of the Supreme Court at Special Term (New York), which granted summary judgment in favor of appellants and declared parts of N.Y. Real Prop. Tax Law § 307 unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Appellant taxpayers challenged the application of retrospective laws to determine how they could prove discriminatory taxation. The court affirmed the order granting summary judgment for appellants. The court held that N.Y. Real Prop. Tax Law § 307 retrospectively sanctioned a real property tax on property by class or type. The court held that a statutory discrimination between two like classes could not be rationalized by assigning them different labels. The court held that the tax scheme was unconstitutional because § 721 extended benefits to certain owners. The court held that the unconstitutionality of § 720(3) was not established because taxpayers had an alternative, non-prohibitive method of proving that they were saddled with an unfair tax burden. However, the court held that § 720(3) could not constitutionally be applied to appellants because they had obtained an interlocutory judgment prior to enactment of the statute.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision granting partial summary judgment in favor of appellant taxpayers. A retrospective law could not overthrow appellant's interlocutory judgment. Parts of the tax scheme that extended benefits to some, but not all, taxpayers were declared unconstitutional. Part of the tax scheme that limited a taxpayer's methods of proof, but did not create an insurmountable burden for the taxpayer, were declared constitutional.


HEADNOTES

Taxation -- Assessment

1. Subdivisions 3, 4 and 5 of section 307 of the Real Property Tax Law, which require inequality petitions to allege that the assessment was made at a higher proportionate ratio to value than that of other property of the same major type as determined by the State Board of Equalization and Assessment and authorize the admission of additional evidence to establish this, are unconstitutional; the class system of taxation is not imposed uniformly against all taxpayers, but only upon those who have pursued a judicial remedy, and nowhere can there be found statutory authority for the tax assessor to assess classes of property at varying rates. The excessive retroactivity of the subdivisions render them unconstitutional [***3] as applied to tax years prior to their effective date, and their prospective operation suffers from similar fatal deficiencies.

Taxation -- Assessment

2. Section 721 of the Real Property Tax Law, which provides that resident owners of structures containing three dwelling units or less can introduce any relevant evidence in an inequality proceeding, notwithstanding any provision of law to the contrary, is unconstitutional as a denial of equal protection because it extends to certain residential owners the right to offer evidence which other taxpayers are forbidden to offer.

Taxation -- Assessment

3. Subdivision 3 of section 720 of the Real Property Tax Law, which excludes use of equalization rates to prove inequality and provides that parcel selection and proof of actual sales are the only admissible evidence by which to prove ratio in inequality proceedings, is constitutional.

 

992 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


D. Lambert Railing Co. v. County of Suffolk


Action Nos. 1, 2


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Second Department


80 A.D.2d 42; 437 N.Y.S.2d 409; 1981 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 9742



April 6, 1981 



DISPOSITION: Two judgments of the Supreme Court, Suffolk County, entered May 29, 1980, and July 28, 1980, respectively, reversed, on the law, without costs or disbursements, and complaints dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant county sought review of the judgments of the Supreme Court for Suffolk County (New York), which found in favor of respondent subcontractors and sustained their argument that 1974 N.Y. Laws 944, 945, were mandatory in authorizing extra compensation for both petroleum derivative and steel products.


OVERVIEW: The legislature enacted 1974 N.Y. Laws 944, 94, upon a finding that the energy crisis had unfairly injured contractors that dealt with state and local governments because of the unexpectedly large postbid increases in the cost of petroleum derivative and steel products that were to be supplied under their contracts. The subcontractors later sought extra compensation that was allegedly authorized under the statutes, and the county refused to make any price adjustments for the steel products that the subcontractors had contracted to supply. The subcontractors then brought an action upon the county's refusal. The trial court found in favor of the subcontractors and sustained their argument that the statutes were mandatory in authorizing extra compensation for both petroleum derivative and steel products. The court reversed the judgments, by holding that the subcontractors were not entitled to the extra compensation for both petroleum derivative and steel products because the statutes unambiguously demonstrated a legislative intent to vest discretion in the various government contracting agencies.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgments, which found in favor of the subcontractors and sustained their argument that the relevant statutes were mandatory in authorizing extra compensation for both petroleum derivative and steel products.


HEADNOTES

Municipal Corporations -- Bids and Bidders -- Price Adjustments Due to Energy Crisis

In actions by subcontractors for extra compensation for steel products they had contracted to supply defendant county, which compensation was authorized by chapters 944 and 945 of the Laws of 1974, which were enacted upon a finding that the energy crisis had unfairly injured contractors dealing with State and local governments because of the unexpectedly large postbid increases in the cost of petroleum derivatives and steel products to be supplied under their contracts and authorized affected public contractors to pass along part of these increases under certain circumstances through price adjustments to the contracts, the complaints are dismissed; by resolution, defendant county determined to avail itself of [***2] the right provided by such legislation to make such supplemental reimbursements, but only to the extent that extra compensation was sought for asphaltic road materials, and since the permissive language used in the legislation reflects an intent to vest discretion in the governmental contracting agencies, the discretion vested in the county was not improperly exercised, inasmuch as there are facts which can reasonably be conceived to sustain the classification.

Independent Church of Realization of Word of God, Inc. v. Board of Zoning Appeals


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Second Department


81 A.D.2d 585; 437 N.Y.S.2d 443; 1981 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 11072



April 6, 1981 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner church appealed from a judgment by the Supreme Court of Nassau County (New York) that dismissed the church's petition to review a decision by the respondent board of zoning appeals that denied the church's application for a special use permit.


OVERVIEW: The church acquired property and filed an application with the zoning board for a special use permit in order to use the property as a religious retreat house and church with facilities for 40-50 permanent occupants. The board of zoning appeals denied the application finding that the church's use of the premises did fit within the requirements of the ordinance for churches or retreat houses. The church commenced a proceeding pursuant to N.Y. C.P.L.R. 78 alleging that the board's decision was arbitrary, capricious and unconstitutional. The special term court dismissed the petition concluding that the use being made of the premises was not a use permitted by the ordinance. The church appealed. The reviewing court found that the premises was not being used as a church for public worship because the building was not open to the public for worship or any other purpose, and that the number of its permanent occupants as a retreat house exceeded 10, the number permitted by the zoning ordinance. Whether the ordinance was unconstitutional was not an issue for the reviewing court to resolve. The decision was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The judgment that dismissed the church's petition was affirmed, with costs.

 

994 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


People v. McMillen


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Third Department


80 A.D.2d 966; 438 N.Y.S.2d 627; 1981 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 10872



March 26, 1981 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment of the County Court of Chemung County (New York), which upon a verdict convicted defendant of burglary in the third degree and possession of burglar's tools.


OVERVIEW: While on early morning patrol, a police officer observed the door of a local bar ajar. As he approached to investigate, he heard noises coming from within the bar. Drawing his revolver, he ordered the person inside to come out, and as defendant did so the officer asked, "Who are you?," to which defendant replied, "Lennie Edwards. I'm the bartender here." Both statements were untrue. Defendant was convicted of burglary in the third degree and possession of burglar's tools. Defendant sought review, and the court affirmed. The court ruled that defendant's assertion was admissible in evidence, because the single question asked by the officer did not constitute an interrogation to which Miranda warnings, which were thereafter given, were applicable. The court also held N.Y. Penal Law § 70.06, regarding imprisonment for second-felony offenders, was not unconstitutional on equal protection grounds where, under the Marihuana Reform Act of 1977, appellant's 1971 crime of possessing marihuana had since been downgraded from felony to misdemeanor status. That argument was unpersuasive because at the time that crime was committed appellant's conduct was considered a serious breach.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court, because defendant's untrue response to a police officer's question was admissible since the question did not constitute an interrogation to which Miranda warnings were applicable.

 

995 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Reichler v. New York State Teachers' Retirement Sys.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Third Department


79 A.D.2d 268; 437 N.Y.S.2d 754; 1981 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 9704



March 5, 1981 



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed, without costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent state teachers' retirement system (STRS) appealed from a judgment of the Supreme Court at Special Term, Albany County (New York), directing the STRS to grant a death benefit application filed by petitioners, representatives of a deceased member's estate. The estate had prevailed in a declaratory judgment suit filed pursuant to N.Y. C.P.L.R. art. 78 after the member died while on a leave of absence due to illness.


OVERVIEW: The member was employed by a school district and participated in STRS. She went on paid sick leave due to a brain tumor and later went on an unpaid leave of absence, which was her status when she died. STRS denied an application for a death benefit based on a finding that she did not meet the requirements of N.Y. Retire. & Soc. Sec. Law art. 11. Her estate then sought a declaratory judgment that the death benefit was payable or, alternatively, that the statute was unconstitutional. Treating the case as a proceeding under N.Y. C.P.L.R. art. 78, the supreme court ordered STRS to pay the benefit. STRS appealed but the court affirmed. It rejected the STRS's interpretation of the governing requirement under Tier II that the member was not "in service" at the time of her death because she was on unpaid leave. It held that the STRS's "selective application" of the definition of "service" in N.Y. Educ. Law § 501(19) to Tier II members such as the decedent was unreasonable. It also rejected the STRS's claim that its position was consistent with N.Y. Retire. & Soc. Sec. Law art. 11 as arbitrary and capricious, and affirmed the order requiring that the benefit be paid.


OUTCOME: The court found that the STRS's interpretation of its governing statutes in such a way as to deny payment of the death benefit was arbitrary and capricious and affirmed the judgment below that required payment of a death benefit to the decedent's estate. Having decided the case on statutory grounds, it declined to address the constitutional issue.


HEADNOTES

Civil Service -- Retirement and Pension Benefits -- Death Benefits

A determination denying petitioners' application for a death benefit on the ground that decedent, a Tier II member of the Teachers' Retirement System who remained on the payroll but was on a leave of absence without pay due to illness at the time of her death, did not meet the requirements of article 11 of the Retirement and Social Security Law, was arbitrary and capricious; although members on an unpaid leave of absence due to a physical disability meet the requirement for a death benefit under the express provisions of either the Tier I or Tier III statutes, as a member of Tier II, a death benefit was payable upon decedent's death only if she died while "in service" (Retirement and Social Security Law, § 448), a term which is not defined; the Legislature has expressly made [***2] the term "in service" more expansive for Tier II members (see Retirement and Social Security Law, § 448, subd e, par 1) and there is no evidence of any legislative intent to carve out an exception for similarly situated Tier II members. Accordingly, a determination that decedent was not "in service" was unreasonable and death benefits should be paid to petitioners.

 

996 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


In re Claim of Liss


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Third Department


80 A.D.2d 716; 437 N.Y.S.2d 731; 1981 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 10433



February 26, 1981 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Claimant appealed a decision of the Unemployment Insurance Appeal Board (New York), which affirmed the decision of the administrative law judge (ALJ) sustaining an initial determination of respondent industrial commissioner reducing claimant's benefit rate pursuant to N.Y. Lab. Law § 600(7).


OVERVIEW: Claimant lost his employment as a mail room supervisor under non-disqualifying conditions. He thereafter commenced receiving a federal pension and social security. As he was thus receiving pension benefits in excess of his established unemployment benefit rate, the board, pursuant to § 600(7), reduced his unemployment benefit rate to zero. On appeal, claimant contended that § 600(7) was unconstitutional in that it discriminated against senior citizens and pensioners. The court affirmed the decision of the board. The court held that the statute was not shown to be discriminatory and it clearly passed constitutional muster. The court reasoned that the distinction made in the statute whereby the unemployment benefits of those people were reduced while the benefits of other persons were not was rational and bore a direct relationship to the underlying purpose of the Unemployment Insurance Law, to provide income to unemployed workers who were without earned income.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the board that affirmed the decision of the ALJ sustaining an initial determination of the industrial commissioner reducing claimant's benefit rate.

 

997 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


People v. Knowles


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Second Department


79 A.D.2d 116; 436 N.Y.S.2d 25; 1981 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 9676



February 17, 1981 



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Supreme Court, Queens County, rendered May 31, 1979, affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his second degree robbery conviction entered by the Supreme Court of Queens County (New York). Defendant claimed that although he held his hand in his pocket in such a way as to give the impression that he had a gun, he did not display anything that appeared to be a firearm, so he was not guilty of second degree robbery under N.Y. Penal Law § 160.10(2)(b) (1965).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of second degree robbery under N.Y. Penal Law § 160.10(2)(b) (1965) after he coerced the victim into surrendering property by holding his hand in his pocket in such a way as to give victim the impression that he had a gun. Section 160.10(2)(b) provided that a person was guilty of robbery in the second degree if he forcibly stole property and, in the course of committing the crime, displayed what appeared to be a firearm. Defendant appealed his conviction, claiming that he did not display anything that appeared to be a firearm. The court affirmed the conviction, holding that the fair import of the statute was that an unarmed person was guilty of second degree robbery if he held his hand in his pocket in a way that convinced his victim that he was holding a firearm. The court cited a previous case in which a defendant was found guilty of second degree robbery where he threatened his victim with a real but inoperable gun. The court explained that there was no difference between the two situations because in both cases the victim believed that the perpetrator robber was armed. As a result, defendant was properly convicted of second degree robbery.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decision to convict defendant of second degree robbery. The court held that defendant, by holding his hand in his pocket in such a way as to give the victim the impression that he had a gun, displayed what appeared to be a firearm within the meaning of the second degree robbery statute.


HEADNOTES

Crimes -- Robbery

Section 160.10 (subd 2, par [b]) of the Penal Law provides that a person is guilty of robbery in the second degree if he forcibly steals property and if, in the course of the commission of the crime, he "[displays] what appears to be a * * * firearm"; if a person who is in fact unarmed commits a robbery and, in the course thereof, positions his hand in his pocket in a manner that is intended to convey to his victim the impression that he is holding a firearm, that person has committed robbery in the second degree within the meaning of the statute.

 

998 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


92-07 Restaurant, Inc. v. New York State Liquor Authority


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Second Department


80 A.D.2d 603; 435 N.Y.S.2d 989; 1981 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 10295



February 17, 1981 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner restaurant sought review pursuant to N.Y. C.P.L.R. art. 78 of respondent liquor authority's suspension of the restaurant's liquor license pursuant to N.Y. Comp. Code R. & Regs. tit. 9, § 53.1.


OVERVIEW: The restaurant challenged the liquor authority's suspension of its liquor license, urging that the evidence was insufficient to sustain the finding that the nude dancers' performance was lewd and indecent. The restaurant argued that the regulations prohibiting nude dancing were unconstitutional. The court observed that insofar as the restaurant challenged the constitutionality of the regulations, the action was converted into a declaratory judgment. The court first found that the record contained substantial evidence to support the liquor authority's conclusion that the premises became disorderly by reason of an indecent and lewd performance. The court next concluded that the prohibition against topless dancing in licensed premises contained in N.Y. Comp. Code R. & Regs. tit. 9, § 53.1(s) was unconstitutional. The court found that the absolute prohibition against the presentation of obscene topless dancing contained in N.Y. Comp. Code R. & Regs. tit. 9, § 53.1(r)(2) was not unconstitutional because it represented nothing more than a State's continuing and legitimate effort to accomplish the goal of prohibiting performances that partook more of gross sexuality than communication.


OUTCOME: The court annulled the liquor authority's finding that the restaurant violated a prohibition against topless dancing and declared that portion of the regulation to be unconstitutional. The court declared the prohibition against lewd and indecent nude dancing to be constitutional and sustained the liquor authority's finding that the restaurant's premises became disorderly by reason of such conduct, and remanded for the penalty determination.

 

999 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


County Dollar Corp. v. Yonkers


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Second Department


80 A.D.2d 612; 436 N.Y.S.2d 54; 1981 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 10304



February 17, 1981 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a consolidated proceeding pursuant to the New York Real Property Tax Law to review assessments on petitioner taxpayer's real property for the assessment years 1962 through 1976, the Supreme Court, Westchester County (New York) denied a post-trial motion for relief filed by respondents, a city, its assessor, and its board of review. Respondents appealed.


OVERVIEW: Respondents had filed a post-trial motion for an order relieving them from a written stipulation as to equalization ratios for certain assessment years, and a further order determining that certain classified rates for the city were applicable for those years. The court upheld the trial court's order denying respondents' motion. The court held that the stipulation should not be vacated in part because of the extreme prejudice to the taxpayer. In particular, the taxpayer had given up much in consideration for the stipulation. The taxpayer had commissioned an annual sales study by random sample selection. That study, which took several years, was completed for most of the years at issue at an actual cost to the taxpayer in excess of $ 15,000. The study indicated a ratio to full value approximately 5 to 10 points below the corresponding state rate. In reliance upon the stipulation, the taxpayer discontinued its annual sales study for the remaining years, absorbed the financial loss in trial preparation cost for the study already completed, and withdrew its proposed order to compel selection of parcels. It would be practically impossible to continue the annual sales study.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order.

 

1000 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


People v. Thompson


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Second Department


79 A.D.2d 87; 435 N.Y.S.2d 739; 1981 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 9702



February 2, 1981 



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Supreme Court, Kings County, rendered May 26, 1978, reversed, on the law, and new trial ordered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from an order of the Supreme Court, Kings County (New York), which entered judgment of his conviction for criminal possession of stolen property in the first degree and which denied his motion that the trial court declare a mistrial.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, who was black, was convicted of criminal possession of stolen property in the first degree by an all white jury because the prosecutor had used his peremptory challenges to exclude all black prospective jurors from the jury. Defendant's motion for a mistrial was denied and the trial court did not inquire into the prosecutor's reason for using his peremptory challenges in that fashion. Defendant appealed and contended that he had been deprived of the right to be tried by an impartial jury. Upon review the court reversed the judgment and ordered a new trial. The court held that from all the circumstances, including the prosecutor's use against black jurors, of all of his many peremptory challenges, defendant's race, and the trial judge's perceptions of both the characteristics of the prospective jurors who were challenged peremptorily and the conduct of the prosecutor, there was a substantial likelihood that the challenges in question were based solely on race, and thus the trial court erred when it failed to inquire into the prosecutor's reasons for the exercise of his peremptory challenges.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court which convicted defendant of criminal possession of stolen property in the first degree. The court ordered a new trial.


HEADNOTES

Crimes -- Challenge to Jury

A peremptory challenge may not be employed to exclude a prospective petit juror solely because of his race (NY Const, art I, § 1) and, where defendant can establish a substantial likelihood that peremptory challenges are being exercised by the prosecutor to eliminate potential petit jurors on that ground alone, the initial presumption that the prosecutor's use of peremptory challenges is constitutionally proper is rebutted, shifting the burden to the prosecutor to show, in response to inquiry by the trial court, that the peremptory challenges in question were not exercised solely on the basis of the prospective juror's race; however, the exclusion of a significant number of black potential jurors is not sufficient, in and of itself, to warrant reversal of a trial court's determination not to make inquiry. Accordingly, the right [***2] of defendant, who is black, to a trial by an impartial jury, as defined by the New York Constitution (art I, § 1), was violated when his timely motion for a mistrial, based on the prosecutor's alleged misuse of all of the substantial number of peremptory challenges exercised by him to exclude blacks from the jury, was denied without an inquiry by the trial court into the prosecutor's reasons therefor, although, considering all of the circumstances, there was a substantial likelihood that it was done solely on the basis of race of the challenged jurors; defendant's conviction must be reversed without regard to the quantum or quality of the proof of his guilt.
